And if the pain has spread to the thigh or leg, make an instrument that burns according to what you have done in the hair; and this is the way of the hot stick, and I have written or described the correction of medicine.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	1. Take alkaline and live ashes, as much of one as the other, and mix them together, and put them in a new earthenware pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	1. If there is a small hole in the bone that is not pointed with a razor and can be entered; then put another pot well filled, and add alum and chalk and sugar until you have two of the powders you want to have in your hand; then leave it until the water drips out of the ague and chicory or can be poured, then take all of this, and mix it with salt and alum as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	When the fire is applied and it is maintained in the wounds of medical knowledge and other cauterizations, it causes a work that resembles fire, and if other medicines are used that are well cauterized, such as honey and anacardium and chalz with soap, all these things melt together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	Galiens tells us of a remedy by which some were cured of the pain in the shoulder and sciatica, and he says that no other remedy is needed, and that it was cured in one session every time this remedy was applied, and he was bathed as he instructed afterward.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And then in another way, you should make the patient lie down on a hard and dry bed, and rub the wound with a little grease, and put it on the shoulder, the thigh, and the leg where the pain is, and tie it; and leave it for three hours and according to the quantity that the patient does not feel the pressure anymore.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then I let it enter the bath as much as the chest is raised, and then I let it enter the bed, and the pain will leave all and be cured.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And advises that no one should use such cauterizing medicines after the evacuation of blood.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	When Diascorides says that if the scientific vein is cauterized with the fleece of a goat, it helps; and it must be done in a certain way.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take the fat and make it into oil, and put it in the flask that is between the little finger and the other which is called the fosphile.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	After drying the goat hair, and burning it until it is charred, and then putting it on the wool, and leaving it as long as it remains stained; and do this again and again until you think that it will reach the skin, and that the pain will cease; and this way of cauterization is called "cauterization with goat hair".
de la dolor dou dos	From the pain of the back door
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether by squeezing or drumming or too much evacuation, or from the appearance of cold expanded matter, in none of these appearances is cauterization justified, rather it should be used for those coming from the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary after the patient has been freed from bitter pills or other appearances, that you cut on his back, wherever the pain remains, three lines of "enche," and in each line V cauterization or more according to skill and the amount that the patient can bear; and make the cauterization according to the cauterizing instrument called "points"; and if you see, make III cauterizations or IIII on the clavicle knife according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	Many times this disease comes to children, and the signs of the beginning are that they become narrow-eyed when they sneeze, and cry; and you see the spine of their back and the appearance that comes from the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and it is cured, if the cauterization is done on the burner according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	If the cauterization makes every part of the spine even.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see, if the cauterization is done at the end of the spine by pricking two or three lines, and they are points close to each other.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After curing the limb until it is healthy according to what we have said, and you should not perform a fire cautery on the skin that is in the flesh of the neck.
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When pain in the joints comes from moisture that is expanded to every member of the body, and when pain comes in the foot, which they call "gout" properly, and when it is cold cause and medicines do not cure it, then it is cured by cauterization in this way: make a cut through the joint of the foot, and the cauterization should be olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	If it seems that you are pricking at the face with sharp nails, then perform a burn with the entire burn as claimed "point".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	If the pain comes to the thigh and other joints, and this happens many times, then perform a burn on each thigh III or IV of each part, at the entire olive cauterization; and if you have skill for more, but do not hold your hand too long as much as the pain may be.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	If the pain descends to the thigh and to the back, then apply the burn we have described in this chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	1. If the pain is in the hands, then I make points every second line; and if there is no more pain, then I make points on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pain comes from the wrists or elbows, then cauterize each part, and govern the patient's behavior with medicine.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	1. If you make the patient govern their behavior and purge impurities, then they will be healed by God.
de la routure dou syfac	1. of the rupture of the facial skin
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	1. If the rupture comes in wrinkles, and the blisters descend as coins and it is novel, then it is necessary that when you see it curing, it does not mix with the other; and that it uses things that soften the belly, if it comes down from his belly; after which you place it on his back between your hands, and command that he licks his hair as much as it is repaired, and pulls it to your two, and signs that it closes the rupture on the bone of the other hand, and in all a sign that is like half of a circle around the other corners; then wash the cauterization with the form:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	As long as it is white and feels cold.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then shape the dough with your hands; and guide your hand so that they do not return; and work well on the thighs, and put the cautery at the sign of all your hand, and hold it right and as far as you can reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, then continue again until you touch the bone; and be careful that the dough does not seep while you are making the cautery, that you do not burn it; and so that the malady does not kill or another harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And you should know that when you do not come close to the bone with the cauterization, your efforts are in vain.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it is necessary that the cauterization of children be subtle according to the measure of the bone, and also great for adults; after three days, cure the wound of the thorn as much as possible, as long as the burning is not too deep; after other injuries as soon as they are healed, and gently lie on his back as long as the wound is well soaked; and it is necessary that his clothes be loose for a long time, so that the dirt does not come out when he gets up to relieve himself in the chamber.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	After forty days, when he wishes to rise, he will find a well-made girdle around him, and after forty more days; let him rest, so that he works quickly and drinks too much beer and honey, and braids his hair too much; and when he performs this instruction, he is completely healthy.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will say after the surgery in his chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the rupture of the stomach
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When ruptures occur in other stomachs and are known, and you see that they do not grow any more, one should re-cauterize according to the quantity, and it should be the third angle according to this form; after the treatment according to what we have said; and no ancient has said that one must cauterize at the cautery with three angles according to this form.
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	1. However, the first sign of the joint is the elbow and I make a line for the widest part of the fracture, and another one, and hold your hand with both hands for all the cauterization clamps.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	2. However, the first cauterizations are more gentle and less painful.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	3. with no pain in any limb.
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	4. When pain comes in any limb, whether from cold or wounding, and this pain lasts for a long time, and medicine does not help, then it is necessary to cauterize at the cauterization point called "points", and the cauterization should be according to the length of the affected limb and its thickness, its flexibility, its location of torsions and its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If the patient is healthy after the first burn, that's good; if not, restart the burn at another spot, because it is customary to die in the member that is proximate, since it must be burned as many times as the maudlin allows.
de meselerie	of masculinity
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The man is aided by the burn once and the disease that comes from the putrefaction of flesh and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	Can you see the burning, when the disease is at its beginning, and if it is cured according to what we said in the division, and does not end or tire, and you doubt that corruption will spoil all the maudlin, therefore I make the following burns on the head: I cut off the head, and the other at the front of the neck at the end of the cheeks; and I touch the corners, and the buttocks at the heel; and it should last as long as the bone, and as long as the sweat comes out so that the vapors of the large humors can come out; and the burn is made on the nose according to what is before.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules; et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	1. If the scald is scattered everywhere; it is obviously present, if you cauterize the wound with these cauteries that we have mentioned or chief, and the cauterization is in one place, and the cauterizations on the shoulder point, and on the back of the neck, and on the crupier and the other delicate parts, and the wrists, and the tendons of the ankles, and all the joints of the hands and feet, and the fissures of the hands; and you will find nerves that are located below the skin, which you should not burn, and never made a cauterization on the bone of the elbow, and the other on the stomach bone, and the other on the liver bone.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	When you perform more cauterizations, the patient benefits more and does not feel pain in the cauterization as much as they should because the body is already corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that the cauterization be large and small according to the limbs and joints, according to what you will find in the manner of irons.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After treating the leg with flour several times with honey and other remedies until it is healthy.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the leg is infected in any member and is treated with medicines and oils and plasters, and it is not healthy, then perform cauterizations on the member according to its size and thickness; and let the cauterization be made in the part of least pain; then treat with ointments as long as it is healthy.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	1. And no time is made when cauterized on the hand, foot, and back, at the end of the nerve that is quieted by the member, and if it is not enflamed; and nothing enters unless one knows the members and the movements of the nerves in the body.
de albaras	2. Of barbers.
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	3. When the disease called "albars" is awakened, and the art of medicine finds nothing to cure it, then cauterize with a cutter one part per quantity of essence of oak, as long as the blenchour is enflamed, and is quiet; then use flour and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and senna and senna of alendron, of each a part; and mix all together, and apply it to the member as often as it is healthy.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment of syphilis by cauterization
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When the sore appears at the beginning, and you see it stop, if it is cauterized with the cautery that seems to form a circle, all around the circumference of the sore.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And the wise say that cauterization is also made in the environment of the sore; and it seems to me that this is not very good, because I fear that it may become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already wanted it to happen once; and the most correct thing is that it be cauterized around, with the cautery called "circling", as we have said in our mouth about cauterization.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	The phrase "de l'enfleure qui ne puet meurer" translates to "the enflamement that cannot be
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When someone has a disease called "adubelati", which delays its death either due to excessive expenditure or insufficient painkillers, or because of old age, and you see it suffering: then the cauterization is performed by touching small cauterizing points; afterwards, it is left alone.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For it will die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see the cauterized part healing, if the cauterization is well made, then.
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	When treating the disease known as "adubelati," place your hand in the environment of the affected area while cauterizing, and ensure that the patient feels relieved in some way, as if the course of the sweat is becoming less intense.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After the treatment, when it is perfectly healthy.
li cure dou feu par fer	The cure with fire by iron.
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another type of disease called "corrodens," which is actually a kind of swelling in the members, as it causes the members to become as dry as the hair.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this disease in the member that can suffer from being cauterized by fire, then sharpen the cauterizing iron according to where the disease is; after cauterizing all parts until all corruption is removed, and nothing remains of it, as everything that is corrupted becomes stone.

Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the cure of burns caused by fire.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	If after three days no healthy char is born, it is good; and if not, continue the cauterization on the parts that are still corrupting.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this disease has never been cured by medical treatment in the place of fire cauterization; but all cauterization by fire is more helpful, and I have already said that the cure of the medical remedy is in the division: take the amount you have.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of wounds that come from pieces
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Many times it happens that wounds come from pieces that cause a disease called "closed" according to our understanding, and it is a large thing that must be avoided.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cauterization of this disease is done in two ways.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	It is to know that cauterization is by fire, and cauterization with hot water.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Cauterization by fire is when you heat it and cauterize with hot water, as if it were a pin of wheat, and it is made of iron in the size that can burn all parts, and have subtle margins; after you put it all on the nail, and turn your hand around the nail until it comes to the point of the nail; and it leaves for three days until it starts to exude pus; then I make a poultice of well-cooked, raw eggs with salt, and leave the poultice all night, and the nails will be pulled out of their roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then, treat the wound with ointment, applying it as soon as it is healthy.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if the wound becomes infected many times, and in the hands and fingers, then it is necessary that you have a cauterization of hot fire; and it should be done in this way: take a piece of iron or steel, or a thorn from a bush, and tie it to the nail and the hinge, so as not to have warts; then place the iron on it so that it burns everything around, then put a little hot water, and hold your hand well, and press your hand when turning so that the margin of the iron touches the root of the nail, and you will find the hot fire way smoothly at the root; then suffer the pain of the hot fire for a little while, then let it go, and it will fall off all its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	I will create a subsequent after this, as long as you are aware of all these things that are in the course, then I will cure the wounds that enter char.
li cure dou trembler	I will cure those who tremble.
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee; et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	If any tremble from cold, or fever, or other, then it is necessary that you make four cauteries or four on the back, one cauterization between each spike; and one cauterization or a point, and at the stomach with the olive cauterization; if they continue to tremble, and recover from the disease of the cold.
des pustules puans	of pimples painful.
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	There is no occasion for the appearance of blisters or pustules, which come from large, corrupted materials.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	If it is necessary to do a fire cautery as soon as the blisters or pustules appear, use a subtle cautery of mithridate wood, or if the point is seized by fire, or the root of Aristolochia, or in a lenticular cautery.

And never do cauterization at the beginning when they appear in this way, as it will not cause them to grow forward, but it is disrupted by the superfluity that comes, and they are cured; but it must be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	When the arrow is captured
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times there are great sanguinations of blood from the arrow that is stuck in the wound that comes to the pardefuers, or to the incision of the abscess, or to the fire cautery of the member, and similar things; and it is a terrible thing to enchant.

And if there is none, then whenever you have to put your index finger on the wound of the vein, and hold it as tightly as possible until your finger is calmed by your thumb, and no more pain; then put the olive-oil cautery on several small and large ones until they are all red; then I, or according to the size of the wound and the leg you hold, hold the cautery against the vein or where you hold your finger, and hold the cautery as long as the vein is not restrained.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	If it hurts when you pull on your child's vein, and the cauterization ends, then quickly take another one that is hot.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And continue to do this one after another until the wound is fully healed; and be careful not to burn the nerve that is sensitive, and avoid other harm to the patient; and you should know that as soon as the artery is without cutting, it cannot well reddish immediately when the artery is large, if it is not by one of the four methods we have mentioned: either by cauterization or extraction if it is properly treated, or by tightening with thread, or by medicines placed on it that can cause redness and swelling; and it should be tied and extracted as soon as possible.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever will tightly mend the wound with threads or to burn things on it, or other similar things, should not profit from it without being harmed.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if there is none, and there is no medicine present, then he should put his index finger on the wound as we have said, and firmly press until it is painful in the wound and in the vein; and he should not move, but his finger should be cold often that it is not frozen and swollen and painful; and he should prepare the tools beforehand for cauterization and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here comes the first sentence to translate: "In this is the second book of surgeries
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	For the first chapter of medicine, we have told you about all diseases that require cauterization or burning, and their causes, effects, and forms of cauterization; and I will go to this chapter as my own way because it is lighter to carry when one goes.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	However, before I begin this, it is necessary that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first cauterizations, and for this reason greater caution is required.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I advise you not to attempt foolishness.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many methods of people come in treatments.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	If they come from those who have died so easily by the force of their disease, and the greatness of their malice; and these must be feared.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And those who say to you: "Wait, I am here"; and the disease is disdainful.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	It is only necessary that you allow those who come to you who have this manner, but put more trust in your honor than in your covetousness, and do not believe everything, but wisely of what you are certain, and what you can have taken and lost; and use prognosis and indication in the cures of your maladies as for salus so is converted; and this will help you to this good reputation, glory, and memory of long time.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Three years' advice, Our Lords give you understanding and rightness of mind, and if you will seek help from the holy inspiration of her hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or I have commanded this chapter in determining by cauteries, according to which cauteries are before or after the chief joints, because you will find it more easily what you will do.
dou chief plein d’aigue	A full chief with sharpness.
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Experts say that this disease comes from time to time in children at the breast, and when the nipple is pulled too hard on the child's chest; and never has it been found that it is caused by anything else.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease as being in children, and to these that I have seen it caused death; and for this it seems to me that I should mention the opening of the vein in part of the treatments.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I have seen an infant of the head being swollen, and the cheek grew every day until it could not support itself; and it was so much moisture that it caused death, and this moisture is assembled between the skull and the bone, between the ear and the skull; and the veins are such when the moisture is between the skull and the bone, and the abscesses are small, which you should cut out of the cheek a large incision; and so long as the moisture persists, the form of the spatulum will be:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more intense, and the abscess is larger, then I make incisions in the manner of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture reaches the bone, and you see the commissures of the chief overstretched in each part, and the wound gushes out when you press on it with your hand, and this has not been noticed before: then it may happen that you have to cut off the head III times according to this way:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, remove all the moisture.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After removing the dressings and powders, and applying wine and oil, and leaving it on for five days; then remove it, and treat the wound with poultices and compresses, and leave the head even, and then sew the dry flesh together as much as possible until the member is comfortable and healthy.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of incision is to look at or open the large opening of the abscess, and the assembled angle; for it is never in front; never on the back; never on the left; and never on the right.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Make sure the size of the abscess opening and the angle of the arrow are according to what you can manage; and do not block the artery; and come down with blood loss, if the patient dies due to blood loss and evacuation of pus.

If the artery does not bleed when pressed, then measure the amount of blood that spurts out, which should be about three drops; if it continues to bleed, pour some oil on it and press hard until the wound stops bleeding; then look at the wound: if the blood does not stop flowing from the bone point, if the incision made does not reach the bone, then strain the wound and sew it, and keep the wound clean until it heals.
de emigrainne	The first sentence to translate is "de emigrainne
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When the head begins to ache, and the fever rises, due to moisture in the tears and sweat on the temples, and sometimes other symptoms appear, and it is treated with medicines and all that does not benefit, if we strangle the arteries of the temples and cauterize, as we have experienced.

puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés. And draw out five sancdes of VI c/, and if the artery is large, then it will be done by drawing it through two strong silk threads of double thickness, so that nothing comes before the wound, and comes off with the blood; then cut off the superfluity that is between the II liiens in that hour, and then, if you see, if the cauterization is hot enough to burn the bone as much as the chiés are cooped; and this is the best work, if the malaide has no fever and is of warm complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the fire cautery is help to finish the moisture: because it is of greater help to the moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	For it is necessary to extract the arteries with soft cloth and make good tents; and when you loosen them, if you are careful with dry medicines that make water flow, and tents as much as possible, until they are healthy; and if there is no cort of the artery as you do, then if you have to use cauterization or the patient's arm which is not yet inflamed, and make it cool with cold water as much as possible, and hold it so that it does not freeze, and if you are wounded and lighter in the extraction of the artery than in cauterizing the vein that you cut with II part, but the cuts should be sharp to last longer without causing more pain.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the head of the shoulder is too loose, it holds less tightly.

dou reume des eulz	The first sentence translates to: "He takes off the hairs.

de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the earache
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that affects the ears is one of the four things: grains, beasts, mines, or similar things like that; or seeds, such as wheat, beans, peas; or things that flow, such as a rheum and a cold and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it affects the ear with a piercing or in some other way, and it does not fit well in the ear, do not make the ear hot.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the piercing, if no drop of violet oil or mender's oil comes out, then extract it; and I make the wound clean, and it snores when exhaling that comes out, and put on the ear pieces of linen or wool; and the ear is in the desus.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	This treatment often comes out once; and if it does not come out, then extract it with forceps as fine as possible, and the form is like this:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer. If she does not jump from all these things that we have said, and you continue to press on the ear even if it causes spasm, and the manner of flicking is that you first clean the scalp with the patient's hand, and draw out the pus according to its strength, then hold the patient's hand between your hands and turn the ear towards the root, and make a small cut at the edge of the ear in the grease or where it hangs down; and the flick should be as a moon, as you go to the pinna, then the bone according to your strength, and the saliva drips into your mouth; and the cure until it is healthy.

If it does not hold in place, it's a waste of time. de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the fever of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien. de la char des papieres	Of the parchment's folds
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This is the first line to translate:
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if it is not cut, then the cautery of the fine cautery lenticulaire subtil, and the cautery after the incision is worthless; and they are repeatedly repaired, with nothing coming from their roots; and when those roots are cauterized by fire, they are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of the gresle
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many things come in papers from the eyes that seem rough and hard in their form and their strength, and for this disease is called "granulation," and it is an assembly of large moisture in the paper on both sides; the treatment is as follows: first, when the granulation stops on one side and the other, it is a light thing to know; then make it larger, then scorch each part slightly, then take it with tweezers, and cover.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot perceive it with your senses, a little paper, if it causes no harm to the patient; and if it is sharp, if it is assembled with stitches, and cured as much as possible until it is healthy; and if it is small, if it does not require force, because the restoration of the surrounding skin will be sufficient.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the snow is hanging down from the edge of the ear towards the part below, if reversed, and the snow is grasped with tweezers, and is pressed from both sides; and if the paper is moved by incision, it causes no harm; and when the snow is clamped, if the salty tears are lifted from the eye that rejuvenates as much as possible until the patient is healthy.
de la graisse des eulz	Of the fat of the hairs
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a grease that is made from the papers of the sheets, and this happens more as children become men, and they grieve for their hair, and they come to the baths in the mornings, and they cannot see the light of the sun because the tears flow to their hair; and because they sleep on it, they soak their pillows with the moisture that exinach produces, and their appearance becomes covered with the grease.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the hair between your fingers and feel the exinach enter your hands.

And the manner of the cautery is that the physician puts his finger in the patient's mouth; then he takes a cloth and makes a circle according to the quantity of ointment contained in each part, and puts it on; and presses with both hands, so that the ointment is assembled in the circle; then they make a small cut in the skin at the corner of the mouth, not larger than the wound made in the gum of the mouth; and then they sew it tightly so that you can see the wound; and in other positions, the wound comes from the cut, according to the shape of a piece of greasy white fat.

des poilz des papieres	of the papers' hairs
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When papers grow hairs that are not their own, and are awakened, they cause harm to them, and bring on diseases such as tears and the softening of papers and albugines, as long as it is due to the destruction of the hairs; and the cure is done in four ways: either by burning together with fire, or by medicine according to what is before or in the chapter of cauterization, and is made by cutting and sewing or by nails, according to what I will say.

Then, use a sharp knife to cut through the hair on one side of the natural hair roots as they grow, then cut the nail at one of the two angles. puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then come those who overcome with equal force according to the form that is here:

Then come those who overcome with equal force according to the form that is here: If you cannot hold the nails, and the thing is not equal, then take a needle or a thread, and pull it out; and take another thread of about the same length as the largest one, and the smaller one, and assemble the threads evenly; then gently press with your hand evenly, and gently sew all the seams where you have cut, until it is healthy; and if an abscess comes to your incision, so that the pain is relieved and the swelling decreases; and never come that the hair of the paper is converted: if you use what we have said about the incision; but the stitching on one side and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui. S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it is late, and the wound has forces, then treat as soon as possible; and if the wound is infected, and the paper is raised, and the hair does not grow back, and this is the shape of the two canines you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of long and wide:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil. Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve. de la porriture de l’oil	Of the oil's fatness
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease, which is called "aleacrati" or the oil comes in two ways: one natural, and the other unnatural.

de l’ungle de l’oil	Of the finger of the oil

des voines des eulz	2. of veins of hairs

de la fistule de l’oil	Of the oil fissure

dou derrompement de toile uvee	A sudden fall of the eye socket
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When a sudden injury occurs in the eye socket, it opens up and reveals papers as if they were grains of resin, and it is difficult to see; therefore, cover your eyes, and the ovary is such that you can insert an awl at the root of the part of the eye that is swollen and affected by the injury, then insert another awl where there is a double thread of the part of the arm; and perceive, and leave the first awl according to its position; then cut off the double thread and pull out a part of the eyeball, and hold it firmly, and draw out the awl and put on the end of it some ointment in abundance on the wound; and leave it until the threads heal with the eye, and cure the ointment with comforting things as long as the wound is sore; and never leave the wound without the eye being surrounded by a circle of cloth, as long as it is sore.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the hairs grow long and even, if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the oil's bag
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease called "alcunnati" is only bags of oil that are assembled in the oil, appearing as if they are descending, but they are not; and the appearance of the dislocation if you do it correctly is to have the patient sit upright and straight, then take the chief between your hands at the second part, and pull it as far as you can see the bag coming to your eyes; then close your eyes, and do not descend and do not be lightened by the light, and see what the patient does as if it were; and if it does not descend, think that it is sore, and if the bag descends from the eye is not assembled as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you hold the patient in your hands, then take the steel probe and make a small incision on the corneal membrane, as far as the continuation of the conjunctive with the corneal membrane and the cornea, until the bow is out; and when it comes out, let it drip into the cold water mixed with honey, or hot or fenugreek is boiled and mixed with honey, then it should be treated with another treatment until it is cured.
des aigues de l’oil	of the water of the oil
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have seen the appearances of water in the division, and when it comes to test; if according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary that you place the oil between your hands crossed, facing the light of the sun, and let the healthy and tight hair grow long; then take the paper of the oil to your left hand if the hairs are on the left, or to your right hand if they are on the right; then take in your right hand, if the hairs are on the left, the instrument called "almagda", or in your left hand, if the hairs are on the right; then place the point of the instrument at the coronet through the hole of a ring in the oil at the smallest part of the coronet; then push the instrument called "almagda" gently, and twist your hand until it pierces the coronet of the oil, and feel that almagda enters the empty space; and it is necessary that the measurement of the almagda hole be at the end of the spiral which is in the prunes; and this is the coronet of the oil; if you see the bone in the paper for the clarity of the corneo-skin, then place the instrument where the oil is, then press the skin deeply along another line after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If it stings now, if the patient sees the physician in front of them and the instrument before them.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After resting a little, if it stings again, open the second way, put on the forceps with the instrument, and when they are fixed and do not move, gently twist your hand a few times; then insert a few drops of ointment through the hole, and remove the instrument.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then apply the ointment with fine powdered rose oil and plenty of blood, and glue it with the healthy ointment.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	Yes, and those who are ours, we put on like a glove with plenty of blood.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the hammer cannot enter the hole due to its hardness, because it has too many hard hairs, then you must grasp the instrument called "alberit", and its form is:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And by perforating only the joint, and not causing too much damage, but making a small hole, as we have said; and at the end of the work, the patient feels lighter, and lies down on his back in the dark room; and he should make no movements, eat light foods, and not move his head to the right or left, and follow his disposition; then he leaves this house in the same state as before, and shows us that he has seen nothing, and then he puts the link back in its place, and we see that he has made this change either during the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary to do this, because the pain increases rapidly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	When the patient feels pain, you should apply oil to the affected area in front of the septum, and follow the instructions provided by the person who is assisting; once it is calmed down, remove the eye and put it on your face or forehead to cover any joint, and be careful in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	Then, go into the house quietly and discreetly, and prepare yourself for this case; be careful, as no disciple should interfere in this situation.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And some came to us who were from Yrach, who told us that in some places it was done for the almagest, but we have never seen anyone do it on our land, nor have we ever read about it in ancient books; and by chance, this is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the appearances of the forms of amalgama, because those who do not know them by sight; and they are truly:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And be the head of this very subtlety, and the tail in three angles.
de la char sor le neis	of the cross and the nails.
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	No time are born or nails of crosses different, and if there are any that seem like scorpions at the mouth of piers; and if it is such or has a cross enchanced with foxy color, and if it is a cross of bone color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In that case of these crosses which are not enchanted, it is necessary that you place the patient between your hands facing the sun; and operate on the nostrils, and moisten the horns on those crosses, and pull them out; for fear that you do not hold them too tightly on one side, until you see that the cross is all out.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there is nothing else that can be done, if you examine all the struments subtly and lightly, without causing any harm; and if it does not overturn you, or cause an apoplexy, if it seizes you and you cauterize as soon as possible, before the wound becomes inflamed and all bones are charred, then gently apply ointment or a poultice of wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the patient does not respond, and moisture comes to the palace, signs that it is healthy; and if moisture does not pierce as it should, signs that it has charred in the bone of the limb, or that the struments cannot be cut: therefore it is necessary to bind a thread of linen around a large knot, and be careful with your hands, and place the struments at each nook or less; and put the head of the shoulder on the child's chest as soon as it comes out through the nose, and carry it in an odorous way until it reaches the mouth; and often make the child do this in schools, and it is a light thing for those who see it; then hold the chief that comes through the nose with one hand, and the other chief that comes through the mouth with the other hand, and guide them after each other as we guide the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	1. Do whatever you can to recognize that the newborn's face has become corrupted with that charm, then cut off the male child's penis, cleanse the blood, and moisten the male child's penis with Egyptian ointment, and return it to its proper place in front; do this 3 or more times until all of what was corrupted by the charm is healed; then put a piece of cloth in the penis for as many days as it remains healthy, and if it has skill in drying herbs, use it; and this is the form of the instrument to purify the child's face, or it is used to distill oils and medicines or the like:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And let it be of silver or gold, resembling a hanging lamp, like a cane, and guide it thusly; and if you see, if I make the cane close, and let the ends be flat to expel the grease; and have an handhold at the head for holding it when heating the oil or no liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the charge on the new one
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times it is found at the head of a new disease called "telul", which grows and becomes large, until it is seen when looked at; and therefore it is necessary to cut it at the beginning, and then remove the bone entirely, then place the cautery or burning medicine; and if it is delayed as long as it is large, if it is hard, of a fuscous color, of poor sensation: if it is not touched by iron for it is enchanted, because whenever it is touched, no matter how, there is always great harm to the patient; and if the enchantment is of so much touching, not of a fuscous color, and you see that it can be covered, if the patient is seen and the malaide is cope with little pain, and cure the leu of things drying and restricting.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the shoulder joint is cut and crushed
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	It is said that when a solution for continuation comes from one of these cartilages, it does not last long, and it is rare in any man.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary therefore that if there is no solution in any man, look at whether the wound is fresh all around his vein; and then rest the lips on a girdle, then cure it as soon as it is healthy; and if the lips are already raw from both sides, then shave all the parts that are getting better as they heal, then tie the lips together with a girdle, extract them, and powder them with dragon's blood powder, and incense the cinders; and put on the powder a piece of a plaster of some other soothing plaster, and leave it until it dries, then cure the ointment as soon as it is healthy.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of sewing is as follows: if you assemble the solution, either by needles, as we have said in the abdominal stitching; or by thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	of lip wounds
