A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	The lips of the wounds of the lips are hard and rough, resembling grains of sand, and smaller and larger; therefore, it is necessary to turn the lips, and cut them each time on a different part, and then use the needle after the incision of vitreol wire, as long as it is not stained; and then the leaven of the salve, and cure the leaven of things dry until it is healthy.
de la char des gencives	The first line of the text is "de la char des gencives.
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times, the girdle of the thigh is disturbed, which they call "albulus"; if you can support it with your nails, and the cloth at its root, and leave the wound or the sanc; then put on the leg a vitriol plaster, or other restraining and desiccatives powders; and if the girdle returns after the incision, and many times it happens, if the cloth second time, and cauterize: if it does not return much after the cautery; and these are the forms of the stitches.
des sordens	The next line is "des sordens.
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	1. No times are assembled at the root of the teeth, where the mouth is between the cheeks, gums that are harsh and sharp; and no times is the black and citrus tooth, as long as corruption comes to the gum, and it is the blackened tooth; if it comes that you place the tooth between your hands, and its roots are in your holy hand, and you expose the teeth or the gums openly, as long as it does nothing; and then I make black and green, and yellow and other stains, as they are painted; and if this is at the first reason, it is good; but if not, then resume in the second day and the tooth, as you have done everything; and you should know that the teeth have different forms of estrumens to make them laugh, according to what the demonstration shows, because the raser that raises the teeth has other shapes than those that are raised between the teeth; and these forms and others are with you revealed.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	1. It is necessary when you treat the pain of the tooth that you delay as long as possible and as much as you can, because it should not be otherwise; for it is a substance that is very hot in nature, therefore there is no excuse for not treating it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	2. When the patient is forced to endure treatment, then you must be certain of the tooth's pain.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	3. Many times the pain of the patient's tooth increases, and it must be made certain that the tooth is not sick, and the tooth is treated; and it should not depart from the pain as long as the patient is being treated, because we have already wanted to do this for these healthier ones; and when you are sure of the tooth's pain, if you must cut into the tooth all along its root, then use a sharp tool at first and then use smaller tools; then tighten the nails well in the first place and then in the second, until they are well fixed; and make sure the patient's teeth are well held in your saint's hand between your fingers, and hold them so that they do not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After removing the tooth with a clean break, and if it does not break, then take none of these string-like things and gently pull out from each part, and move it as you have done first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the teeth are felt and pulled out, then it may be necessary to fill them with linen; and if the extraction is done subtly with needles, which does not break the tooth; and it is wise to overturn the girdle to clean the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be well advised that you do not break it, and there remains a part, and the patient suffers from the malevolence of the root, greater pain than the first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	The patient should not attempt to make a cut like the ignorant healers who, with their haste and hardiness, break the skin no time at all, and cause no harm that we have known; but they bring about nothing by the fever of this great disease, either from the roots that they drink, or from the cut that they make, as often as we have wished; and if the wound is deep, cleanse it with wine or vinegar and herbs; and if the poison comes out, which often happens, use vinegar and vitriol; and if that does not work, cauterize.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the wisdom teeth, whether they are still in the gum or not, are long and large incisors, which do not double when you pull the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should be of large size if they do not break when pulled, and they should be made of good iron, and they should have teeth to hold onto.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth.
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root of the tooth breaks when pulled, if it comes that you must put on the gum a soft cotton ball for one hour or more.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	as long as it is smoothed, then it will remove the tines called "alderfri," even if the head seems to be a beard of care; and they should be made in this way like a lime and that is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not come out through all these pricks, then you must pull the tooth entirely out of the root, and then insert the instrument called "athalie", which is a type of tweezer, with this form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And if it is very large and does not break the skin, and if the root jumps through this, it is good; otherwise, if you need help from all the instruments, and the forms come after like this:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you need help from this instrument with two rings, and the form is like this:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other instruments that are in front in the reason of teeth, and this instrument with large pricks, which is like this:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	1. If the bone is too hard to break, and it has few fragments of bones; and others, which are not so easy; and the surgeons use their instruments skillfully, according to what their experience and the disease they demonstrate, because they have some diseases or the ancients did not teach any instrument for the diversity of bones and they do not break at the wrong place or other bones, or they pour, if they seek estruments that I said, and help with gestures, according to what is shown in the figure:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	1. And may be thick and well-held to hold the bone, so it does not break, but can hold and support; and then restore the medicine corresponding to this, and if there is in the bone exudation, and it is small, if all this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not to fit naturally in the gum, and it forms an ugly shape, and in women, if it is broken after the tooth, and it is not straight, and it cannot be soaked or polished: therefore the root; and if it is pulled with the tooth, then use this instrument whose form is like this small tooth, and it should be sharp and hard:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the grip is small and small in hands because of the hardness of the tooth, and this is why you cannot move the others, and if it is visible, then it can be polished, if the part of the tooth is like this form:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	1. And it comes as if the bone of a bird is made like an eagle's claw; and in the bone, the point is small and small in the hands, so that it does not move until it catches hold; then the flatness at the end has no roughness, and the teeth are too sharp and they cut the tongue, if it comes to tightening the string as much as possible, without making the tongue crooked or corrupting the speech.
quant li dent lochent	2. When the point of the bone is small and small in the hands.
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	3. When the point of the bone is small and small in the hands by pressure or by blowing, and the patient cannot press on it as much as it holds, and you should treat them with restrictive medicines, and that is enough; if they are to be restrained by a golden thread, because the silver threads turn green and rot, but the gold does not, and if the thread is too thick or too thin, according to the amount of space between the teeth; and if you see the teeth, if you take the thread and double it between the healthy teeth, then put the ends between the crooked teeth, as long as you see sensibility in the healthy tooth on the other side; then resume the covering from the part where you began, and gently and wisely move your hand, so that it does not move at all; and if your thread is at the root of the tooth, so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then they sew the head of the string to a nail, and assemble it, and place it between the healthy tooth, and put it in so that it does not bend the tongue; and then they let it be tightened as much as possible, and if it slips, or the string comes off, if it is tied with another string; if it stays and holds all its tension, and this is the form of the teeth and the shape of the incisors of the two healthy teeth and the two canines, just as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth is sewn, if it is removed from the gum, again and again, as we have said; and it does not become loose until it is sharp and painful, and never takes on the form of a bone chip, and it is placed in the gum where the deficiency is, and it is tightened as we have said, and stays tight, and lasts long:
de coper lou liien de la lengue	The tongue of the language of the mouth is dislocated, and it cannot be moved, and the patient suffers
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	No time is there ever a tongue that comes out of the mouth or nature, that is not known; or by accident of wounding; and the language is such that you open the mouth of the patient, and it is in its proper place, and the tongue is in its proper position, and it is held firmly by the physician's hand; then loose the nervous tongue as much as possible, until the tongue is dislocated from its place, and if it bite or cut, and it is due to pain, if the upper tooth bites and cuts the lower lip; and hold the tongue so that it does not become too much, for the artery which is out of place; and when you have done, if the tongue is red and swollen, or cold, then place the tongue in a linen tent; and the physician marks each night the patient's tongue, so that the patient may know.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if the dislocation is away, if the joint is not hot, if it is cauterized with a slow cautery, which is good for this; then the care of another care until it is healthy.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it to be red or black or hard, if the patient does not feel it, if it is not touched, because it is gangrene; and if it is deformed into a blindness, and it has moisture, if it flows pus, and it is made with a subtle sponge, and it is delivered from one part and another; and if it is not painful in your wound, if the joint is heated with vitral broth until it is infected, then return to your wound as soon as you can bear everything; then raise the limb easy and soft, and the care of other cares until it is healthy.
des apostemes de la gorge	The first sentence to translate is "des apostemes de la gorge". A literal translation
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Never comes the gorge boces that are called "godath", and they are properly the II amandres, and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, if they are not healthy, then hold: these are small and of colorless, if they do not touch iron at all.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is large, if it does not touch iron at all, then for the loss of blood; but it will remain as long as it is dead, and then you will leave it, or it will break by itself; and if it is of blainche color and the root is subtle, if you have prepared the instrument with copper, but first look at whether the apostemes chalz are resting and are calmed.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then I make the patient stand in the sun, and their head should be in their right state, and they operate the mouth and take the serum between their hands, and press the tongue evenly all around the instrument, regardless of whether it is silver or gold: and it can be fine as some beltbuckles.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Can you press the tongue evenly all around the instrument, and see the incision, if you take the forceps and the needle in the lamb, and draw it as far as you can; and do not bring anything of the cloth with, then close the instrument, regardless of whether it is silver or gold: the handle is curved, and one end to the other, and are very sharp, and is made of iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	If you do not have this instrument present, if you have needles, then the form is like this:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And let it be trenched on one side and named on the other; and when you have cut one of the hairs, if you cut the other in the same manner, and after the incision, heat the blade with hot water, and make it sharp and smooth, and the sutures come out as soon as possible, if you heat the blade with hot water, or if boiling peas are cooked, or if mirtes are fried, and similar things, until the blade is not dampened; then the cure takes place as soon as it is healthy; and no other abscesses ever appear in the mouth except for the two hairs, if they are cut exactly like the two hairs.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with a wound that was not healing in her throat, which is to say it was a small abscess; and she had well closed almost all of the throat, so that the woman could not breathe through the channel that was blocked, and could not drink or urinate, and died if she delayed for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so large that it had been opened twice by the two holes.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I had thus opened it, and found a large piece of bone in one of the holes, and a smaller piece in the other hole, and closed the mouth and pressed the tongue; after opening the abscess in these wounds, and taking out a part, and only a little blood came out, and then the woman was able to swallow water and wine, and continued to cut down on this abscess by long pieces; the abscess grew larger and filled the hole that I had made, so that it could not pass through; therefore I sewed and cauterized the wound: afterwards she did not grow; and I went away from these parts, and only God knew what happened after me.
de l’uve	Of the uterus
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the uterus is drawn towards the vagina, and it is long and thin, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is very large and round, it is called "uterus".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the cut does not profit, and you see that the wound is calmed and subtle, and it is suitable to insert; and the one that is round and not long is assembled and not long; and it is bloody or has a red or black color, and it is suitable to avoid the incision of it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	It is therefore, when you see it, according to the method I have described, of the patient's gallbladder and length, that you should place the patient facing the sun, and press the tongue on the instrument we made note of before; then remove the nail from the eye, and pull out the thread, and cut off the two ends as I said in the incision of the two amandines.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you do not cut too much beyond the natural termination; for if you cut more, it will hurt your voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we said in the incision of the two amandines, and cure as long as it is healthy.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	If the patient suffers from great pain, then it is necessary to use engine for the cauterization of the painful part.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of cauterization is sharp when it is hot fire.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the patient puts his head in your hand and then presses his tongue on the instrument we have mentioned in the chapter of cauterization, and confines with hot live fire, so that it is not too thick or too clear; and by using the edge of this instrument, the form is:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient has a hair or puts medicine on his forehead, as the cat's ear, and places the instrument all over the medicine on the eye; and the patient is grimacing on his chest, if the saliva and mucus are coming from his mouth of the medicine given, if it does not go to the chin and throat, then hold your hand all over the medicine and press on the eye, as much as you see the pain and the medicine bites are eased; and if you see, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and thrust the instrument through the cotton into the medicine as much as the cotton dries on the eye; and do this often, as long as the cauterization is perfect, then let it dry, and afterwards wait four or five hours or six; and if you have skill in re-cauterizing the medicine, if you re-cauterize, and after the cauterization of the mucus around the eye, wrap it in wool, and clean what is outside of the medicine; and be washed with cold water, and cure the gargles as long as it is healthy.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This treatment is safer than incision, only cauterization; if it is treated with fumigation according to this method, take care and yew, oregano, rosemary, chamomile, and all the herbs mentioned, assemble them all or none of them in one pot, and add water, and boil; and it can be well glued with strong earth, and the pot should have the instrument made according to this method:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it can be of silver or gold, and some of the heads are placed in the mouth of the patient as long as the vapor rises to the eye through the canal, as long as the eye is mortified; afterwards it resumes often, as the eye dries, and make sure you do not do this at the beginning of the onset of abscess, because other things also come; and do not do this for the decline of abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	If this instrument is not present, then take a catheter and insert it into the patient's mouth, if the mouth of the patient is too dry; for the crown of the tooth does not cause pain in the mouth, as the crown of the tooth does not grate the mouth, and this is a good remedy together with salvation.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it has happened in the throat, either a bone or a fish spine, or nothing at all; therefore, if you must see what is there, and press the tongue against the instrument until you see the thing; and whatever does not open and is stuck in the throat, it is necessary to make the patient vomit unless the meat is cooked in the stomach; by chance if the thing is cleared through vomiting; or if the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a root of herbage, or a piece of dry bread; and then wrap it with the sponge and then glutinous; and when it reaches the stomach, if it does not come back, and then draw it out; and if it does not come out as we have said, then use the instrument according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	1. And let the patient's head be placed in the chisel so that it may enter more gently into the mouth, and the chisel should be held high above the epigastrium; and guard against touching the epigastrium, as all will suffer from it, and neither the bone nor the instrument should be bent; and it is best that the patient and the tool are bent, because they are both in need of it; if the bend is not made, or if it is made too much, so that it becomes uncomfortable, then it should be adjusted accordingly.
de la sansue de la gorge	2. of the neck of the mouth
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	3. No time is there for the medicine to be effective, as I have said in the division, by the use of medicines; and when it does not help, then look at the patient's mouth with the sun, then press the tongue against the instrument that I have told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	If you see the limb, if it is all of one piece or has fine hairs that are equal in value to this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if it is not worth anything, if you take a fine hair and pull it through the mouthed needle, then pull or cut the hair and make this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And wet the needles every day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take full cold water, wet the eye, and make the mouth, and it feels like it is being sucked in, and move it to your hand often; and if the limb feels cold, then heat.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	If she does not understand as we have said, if the patient is smoking afetide, with the instrument I mentioned in the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, as it will feel like a tar.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the manner of the fumigation if you prefer to use it or if there are charcoal fires, and put the cover of a covering cloth in the environment, and in the other part, place the head of the instrument; then your fumigation is ready, and the patient puts the end of the cane in his mouth, and closes the mouth, so that the smoke does not enter, but goes to the stomach; and the stomach will now hurt, and if it recurs, do the fumigation many times; and suffer the patient's thirst, and drink salty and acidic things, and do not drink any lemonade; and then his labor will be done according to this government.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument used to treat the wound, if it is, when it can be seen, resembles tines of corbels to enter the mouth; it resembles the beak of a surgeon, and has sharpness like lime, so that whatever it takes, it cannot let go; and here is the form:
li chapistres des apostemes	The cautery of the abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	The appearances of the abscesses are, according to what is remembered in this book, and they vary in perforation and size; and there are two ways in which one is in its own appearance itself, and due to it being moist.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And if it is by the legs or they are at the core.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the apostles of his head are different from those of his foundation, and the apostles of his lower limbs are different from those that come in joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if in the apostles one does not know how to perceive, as long as the bow is dead according to its completion; and if for such things it is necessary to perceive when they are thought to be, and do not die until their completion, like those of joints that are delightful.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when apostles come from delightful joints, and they are left as long as they are soft and supple, by chance if the ligament and nerve of the joint are corrupted, because this is due to contraction in that member.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	1. When the incision is too deep and affects the main limb, and you delay the perforation as long as it is still alive, it will harm the main limb; or it is due to the foundation, if the hole is not made until it is dead; and only the incision that feels like it has completed digestion should be made, as the one that is due to the foundation, it will not cause any damage, and it will be long-lasting and form a fistula; and it cannot be cured in a short time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	2. It is necessary that you scrape the wound of the incision that is dead according to its completion, and when the pain is eased, when the fever subsides, when the pain and the bruising are reduced, and there is no debate or agitation in the main limb, and other signs; and it is necessary that you make the wound as close as possible to the base of the incision, and where it was opened; and the wound should be long enough to reach the hand or foot, or in joints and arteries, and in all places where there are no clots.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those that prick, according to the member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in the flesh, if it is large, you should leave the puncture until it has been confirmed in digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you prick before this, and the blood comes out of it, and it is painful to the touch; and by chance they harden the lips and become flat.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if no abscess is found according to the size of the blood, according to what the member can bear.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is necessary that you open small abscesses, small wounds, and great ones according to their appearance; and in large abscesses, large wounds, and multiple fissures according to the size of the abscess; and if in such abscesses or they have to be cut off, and closed, then it is necessary to do so as with a button: and if in such ones that are cut at three angles, and in such ones that are closed like the thorn of a grape, as with abscesses of angry people; and if in such ones that are cut at one angle, and others at other angles and appearances, then they are closed like buttons.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	1. Those who lack a chief, if the superficial abscess is like aposteme, it is necessary that you open it gradually; and when the abscess is large, and the pus is great, and it has filled the entire wound, but only a part of it, then the abscess will subside in the other day, and then nothing more should be done to it; this is repeated many times until all the pus is out. Even if the woman is weak in virtue, or a young girl, or an old man with decayed limbs, it should be treated in this way.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the expectoration, there has been no occasion with the issue from the bowels, that by chance the patient died, and you do not remember it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have discovered the abscess, if the wound is infected, look at the size of the abscess; and if it is a small one, use a linen or cotton gauze; and if it is large, and there is fever, then wrap each in a gauze so that they compete with each other; and if you have cut into a part of leather with the abscess, and it has grown out, then wrap it with fine cloth or ragging of linen threads, and sew it to the bone as soon as possible, and then the skin, and the cure of ointment until it is healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if the dislocation occurs in the shoulder, it may cause you great pain and injury, so take care of your shoulder many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation persists, if it is not governed and treated, and the powders that I have mentioned in my hands in this book, and if you are afraid of the poultice, then you should make sure to put it on and dress the wound with a thin layer of vinegar and olive oil; and if it is like this, and the powder is dry, if you must put the wound dressed with cold water and oil, or with wine and oil warm, as we have said; then remove the poultice and the discharge and the treatment, as it comes, until it is healthy.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	This comes when it is necessary to know about the treatment of abscesses in their entirety: or you have said what one must do before the treatment of abscesses, and now this chapter.
des soros	of sore
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	When the head of the shoulder comes with bites from abscesses, and they are like those in the following ways, as we have seen, and it is like the grape vine, and many are similar.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	It has many that are fat and similar when it is moist, as we have seen with poultry; and if they are hard and rough in the cutting, and there is no doubt that it will not be against it.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	1. And the measurements are such that if you measure it with all the instruments called "entromising," according to its form, whatever it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	2. If it contains moisture, then they will be made longer by the surgeon's hands.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	3. And when the moisture is seen, do not leave the hair that contains it, because it will return as soon as you leave it; then soak cotton in Egyptian ointment if it is present; if not, use warm and wet compresses, and place the wound on another day; and whatever is left of the moisture will be removed.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then the thread resumes as before, on the second day, and the wound, until you see that it does not weep at all; then treat the wound with ointment according to the convenient time, until it is healthy.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the gout holds for a long time, according to this form, it becomes very long; and it gnaws your bones, and scorches them all over, and applies all your care to draw out the fever; and if the artery is opposite, I will do as I have said after this.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And I also treat the gout if it is very painful, and cut it off and cure it as I have said.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And he measures the incision for the abscess and the wound, if it is more gentle, because there are few sutures.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if in any of these incisions or wounds there is no moisture, and these are not from an old woman's nail; and I found the incision as a sharp, rough, and bluish piercing, which could not be cut; and if none were made, it was as good as a piercing.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other incisions or wounds, if these come from the head or chin, and the opening is as far down as possible, depending on the ear; and they are treated accordingly.
des scrophules	The first sentence to translate is: "Ou cautere
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	For the fire cautery, many times there are abscesses at the collarbone, and the screws are removed, and the angles are cut off, and never have any other part been cut or broken, and they are gnawed and twisted with each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scar is properly formed on its side, as we have said, if the wound and the abscess are on the shoulder; and the appearances of these scars are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	It is said that there are certain things that contain moisture, and that there are also malignant things that do not want to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In that case, where you see a good arrangement of the tochier, and it resembles the color of the corselet, and is silent in every part and is not equal to the artery or the conduct, and is not equal to the skin; if it comes that you cut it through, and burn it in every part, and the lips of the keur are burned, and the oncines are also burned, if you can bear it, as we have said in apostles, and the trai is small and small, and you are sure that you do not cut the nerve or the vein, and are not equal to the spatumile or the trenchans, that the hands do not slip, and do not see too soon, that you do not cut anything more than you should.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you prick the vein or artery, and it does not bleed, then put vitrol beads or any powder that remains sanguine in the wound, and stretch the wound; and leave it until the inflammation is soothed and the wound is softened, and it will begin to ooze.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And if the wound is not cleaned, then return to your vein as soon as you have finished; then look at your index finger to see if it has any small pustules, such as blisters or boils.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if the wound is a large boil, then only cut out that boil at its root, but leave the surrounding skin intact with a double strong thread, and let it dry naturally; then apply the cotton wool soaked in Egyptian ointment to the wound, and cure it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	If you manage to cover the entire wound, it is necessary to assemble the two lips of the wound, and then close it now, as there is no excess material due to the size of the wound.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	If you can understand how to cover the root of the tooth and draw it out, and then cut it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those wounds that have excess material should be cut open if possible; and the cut should be made in the same way as the one mentioned earlier, then treat it with ointment and similar things, so that it does not become corrupted; and when the wound is healed, if the cure of ointment causes inflammation, as long as it is healthy.
de squinance	Of the shoulder
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke of the shaping of the jaw; but I have never seen anyone do this in our time, and it is written in their language.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those with dislocation of the shoulder, it is necessary that the incision made, called "epiglottis," be avoided; and no help can be given in this case because all the veins and the pormon of the patient are in the mouth, or in the throat, or in the ears.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the throat, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid the destruction that comes from dislocation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is therefore necessary, when we wish to cut the epiphysis, that we cut it at a distance of three or four circles or one small cut through, between the two circles or according to the quantity of the cut, and not in the cartilage; and then they are easy to section of the epiphysis as there is no char, and the vessels are long.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the masters are too tight, then it extends the jawbone to the entire neck, and then cuts the knot as it comes to the neck; and avoid the vessels of the sinus, if you see nothing, and then cut the face, as we have said; and is demonstrated by the section of the bloody gouche that jumps through the broken bone which is fractured, and by the lack of voice; and leaves the wound overturned a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the hour has passed since the injury, gather the two lips of the wound as much as they can, and press on all sides to touch the cartilage; then administer medicines that make the patient feel better, as long as they are healthy.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim does not do anything until the patient's mouth is completely swollen, and the patient is judged to be dying, and the lack of meat.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Therefore, you must operate on the epigastrium because the patient cannot breathe, and they are dying by the wound, and you must keep them alive; and therefore, the ancients commanded to leave the wound overgrown until the malice of the disease has passed, and it has passed in three days or four. And therefore, they commanded to cut the wound and cure it, as soon as it was cured. And I will tell you what I see.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I see that a maiden is hurt and cut, and she has a piece of cloth in her throat, and part of her neck is cut; and I was called to cure her, and I found her already dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that came from it, and although she did not have much vein or lead to her arm, the blood was coming from the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I quickly examined the wound and cured her as soon as she was healed; and she did not return until she was dead, and then returned to her position; therefore I say that in the cutting of the epigastrium there is no great pain.
de la grosse gorge	Of the large jaw

We have said in division the ways of incision, and the extraction of arrows; and we said the difference between the incision enjambree as rains, and those signs, and in which pike one must over for size; and in the vessel, and in the verge; and I will tell you openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the incision which is more frequent in the bladder in children, and it is a sign that the child's water has jumped from the bladder, resembling its subtlety; and it is open harene, and greets his mother's girdle, and he can many times, and then becomes large; and at the end of these jumps, the children's waters are reduced to IIV years, and it is a grief in viellars, and it is as jones moiene, in those who are between jonesce and viellece; and it is the cure more light in those who have large pike, than in those who have small.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the cure, if we cover the patient first with a cloth, we must clean all the feces that are inside.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it never hurts to press on the wound.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the waist, stand up and move down until the wound reaches the top of the bladder, and never feel any pain in the upper part; then place it between your hands, with your hands on the lower parts of the thighs, if the bladder is completely deflated; then press and touch the wound; if you feel the wound in the vicinity, it is now time to cut along the wound.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier. Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	1. And they go between the bones and the foundation, not in the cost of the opposite side; and there should be three on either side of the incision, and the head should be either at the foundation or the incision, and the tail should be wide enough so that it is large by default, and becomes narrower, according to the size of the incision, not too large; by chance, the pressure if it is at the foundation, that it jumps further due to work; and they check if there is a part pieced or angles, and margins: if they are rough to come out; and if a part is connected, it resembles a glance, and curves, whose end is light.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	For the head, if it has angles and edges, make the size larger; and if it does not slip, then you must pull on the nails that are like a wedge at the top, to hold the piercing so it does not slip; or you may use a subtle instrument under the chin; and if you do not manage to pull it out, then enlarge the hole in the chest, and if it is not broken, then use gypsum to stretch it, and if there are more piercings, then pull out the largest one at the top of the vagina, then cut it, and the rest after that.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	If it is left large, it will become even larger, causing a great wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For there are two possibilities for the patient: either they die, or urine comes out through the urethra because the urine cannot be held; but you should try to draw it out, or cut it with nails, as much as you can until you have completed your task; and when you have finished your work, use frankincense and aloe and dragon's blood ointment, and pull it out, and put on moistened cloths in oil and wine, or in rosewater and cold water to soothe the wound; then tie up the patient at the neck, and do not let the string slip from the knot.

When you dislocate the shoulder, if it is well oiled with oil and vinegar, then apply the first aid remedy of ointment of balsam and basic ointment, until it is healthy.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if the abscess comes into the wound and corrosions, and blood clots in the vein, and this is retained in the urine, which is done in part in such a way that without jumping with the urine: then take your hand in the wound, and extract the pus, because if it remains, it will cause the vein to rupture and bleed; then cleanse the wound with vinegar and iodine and salt, and help in all ways that you know, until it is healthy; and make sure that all the remedies you apply, you tie the thighs together, and assemble the medicines under the arm.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the prick is small, and it is led by the vein, and it is not cut, and the urine cannot be discharged; if the cure of this that I say is otherwise, you should cut it many times, it is an excuse for the size of this cure.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already used this method before.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	I will prepare it according to this form and make it at a 30-degree angle, with one ton.
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take the thread and tie it around the vein opposite the prick, so that it does not get caught in the uterus; then pull the thread gently through the vein until it reaches the prick; and turn the thread in your hand over the prick as much as you can, until you can feel the prick on the other side; if urine comes out, then press your hand on the part of the vein that is exposed to the uterus.

de la piere des femmes	of the woman's wound
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	If there is only one wound in women, and if there are no other times, then the cure is difficult for three things: the first is that by chance the woman is a virgin; and the second is that it is not possible to find a well-known woman who has descended as mires, even when she is cast.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. If a third method is found that by chance there is a skilled woman in this art of hands; and the fourth method if it is that the woman's wound is more than the man's, because it is easier to make a more perfect size, and greater pain it has. And if one must be removed from this, then it comes that you prescribe a wise remedy for the women's life, or a woman who knows a part of the art, and she commands that she does what you command in the inquisition of the wound; and look well if the woman is virgin: therefore it comes that she must fulfill her duty or foundation and seek the wound; and if she is true, if she is constrained by her duty, and the midwife recommends that she fulfills her duty or with the midwife, and who wants to press her left hand on the bladder forms.

si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	If you suspect any deformities to know the outcome.

And if it is not bleeding, then put vitrol on the wound and hold it for an hour until the wound is no longer bleeding; then return to your work, as long as the wound is firm, and have estrumens as I mentioned in the extraction of the wound to help you in your work. de hernie carnouse	of hernia cancer
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	1. The ramices aquose are nothing more than an assembly of moisture or white soap, which is removed from the hair roots, which contains the epididymis; and is called "soap"; and it has never been properly in the fabric of the epididymis, if one takes care that it is another organ; and this is the skin between the white soap that we have said; and they have not been seen without.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	2. And the generation of this ramice is from fibulature that comes to the hair roots, and it is expanded by that matter.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	3. de l’aposteme des coions	Of the abscess of the thighs
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Sutures that in the cutting of this ramus cause pain in many cases, and I think it is better to leave them; and I will tell you the procedure and the appearance of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say therefore that all abscesses come from wounds and also from arrows; and this is in many cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	It is to know that the abscess is caused by superfluous acrid and sharp matter, which is expanded in the wound or by percussion; and the color of the abscess is according to the color of the wound; and there is no pain, and it is a grievous abscess, and sometimes it is grayish-green and purplish, and without any blood from an artery or vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is of an artery, if it is cut by the disposition of an abscess, when you press on it with your two hands; and only then can you touch it.

dou chastrement	The first sentence to translate is "dou chast

The first sentence to translate is "Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi," which means "As for the chastisement, it has been forbidden in our law." The fourth sentence is "et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes pour nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes." which means "and the other, because we often help certain animals with chastisement, such as goats and sheep, and rabbits and others.

des apostemes de la marris	Of the patient's abscesses
