Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	Therefore, in this treatment, it is necessary to treat the aposteme chaut that comes in the patient, which is not the same as other abscesses; and if you see the wound, look to see if the aposteme is red at the beginning of its appearance, and whether there is chalor and fievre, and if it becomes red, you should see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	1. Therefore, do not hurry to remove the splint, but make him endure as long as the pain is soothed; and then place the patient on his side, with two pillows under his head, and support his back and assemble his limbs in their proper position; and let his thighs be expanded, and put his knees against his chest, and tie them well with a belt; then move the instrument towards the left side, and after that comes the form; and it is necessary that when you see him using this instrument, you fix the rite first to know the proportion of the marrow, so that what comes from the instrument does not exceed what it should, and does not cause the patient pain; and if it is larger, then it is necessary to cover the proportion of the marrow with cloths, so that the patient is not grieved; and it is necessary that he places the end of the instrument at the root, and marks the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	1. When the wound is open and it is touched with the hand, if it sticks to the head, apply warm ointment to the swelling; and when the bow is visible, if it is necessary to put in the wound soft tents in oil rose or orange-scented oil; then place the tent for the wound at the end of the marrow, and place it on the marrow and the clean, soft, warm, or cool pimple that has been cooked; then the cure after two days of dressing, as long as it is healthy; and never lift the marrow and the wound by a cloth of warmth and honey, and then with warmth or the roots of lilies and aristocratic plants are cooked; then repeat the dressing.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is closed in the marriage, then it comes that you must not cook with iron, but cure as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	Mastery is first in the dance that she knows the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs if you see the woman press against the bed, and desire to smell the aroma: therefore, haste the children to be born; and you should know that these children are according to the figure natural, and are from his own offspring, and the second one with him; and when you see these signs, it comes to gently press his belly, if he gives birth quickly; for when he descends from his head, if he is with his second one, and is monied by good cleanliness, and that which comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it has never come upon its own parts, and comes to the heart or shoulder, and the hands, or to the belly or stomach, and is converted by chance in his neck, and through other malicious figures; if it is skilled at the dance that it is wise and subtle in these things, and warns against error and deceit, and I will show you all the figures to help.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes to its father naturally, and the woman gives birth painfully, and his virtues are weak, if he is placed on a stool or the women hold him; and if his nature is olive oil or fenugreek is cooked, and then dance between his two little spatula, which is this form:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	1. And take the second part, and hold it against his finger as much as the moisture that is in it; and then press the belly of the woman as much as the children descend, and if they do not descend, then it is necessary to close the woman's muscles with ointment of fenugreek; then apply and suture and tie the mouth and nose for an hour: if now the child comes out.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	2. And if the hands come out first, then it is necessary to gently open the wound a little at a time; and if they do not enter, then the woman should sit on the bed, and lift the feet up; then lower the bed on the ground, and examine the woman to see if she does not bleed standing; and if the hands cannot be inserted, and the child is dead, then it is necessary to cut the fingers at the point that is in front of it, and take out the child, and reset it gently.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	Of the child's foot issue
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes to his feet, if it is necessary to put on shoes; and then they are tied tightly; and then the legs are pulled and stretched as much as possible; and then the shoes are put on.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	Can it jump high, if commanded, and made to run faster; if it jumps, let God help it.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not jump, as we have said, if the shoes are tied tightly, as much as possible, according to the natural form.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it is light.

de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	2. of the issue of the child from its groins.

de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	From the issue of the child who comes out wide with a hand

de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	2. In the same manner for all the second-degree burns.
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	3. de l’issue des gemelz	Of the issue of the twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	It is said that twins are born many times, and never at the third or fourth birth; and this is a strange thing, and not often seen.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Two things are strange, and do not live long, I know what it is, that they are multiplied, and are born by the force which decides them, which is like the bud; and never issue naturally as all come at once, as we have said.

de l’enfant mort	Of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	I see a woman who is pregnant and had lost her children, then consulted another and was found to be dead by the other.

je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called for the cure, and I thought it long, and could not open the wound.

Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was surprised much, because the belly has no bones.

dou ramener la marris a son leu	To bring the shoulder back to its place.

Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	1. This instrument is all around, and its appearances are multiplied; and when you see them, the more you work, the higher the price for them in quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	2. If you do not despise the instrument because you have not seen it, for its necessity is not easy to understand.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	3. When the second child is held in the womb, if you command the midwife to let go of the hair, and then pull it out, and make your hands go to the mouth and nose; and if she jumps because of this, well and good.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If the child does not cry, and I can, I will suckle or give a drink, and I will put herbs that may open the mouth of the child's mouth, such as mint, rue, anise, chamomile, calamus, and centaury; all these herbs, or none of them, are cooked or can be boiled over fire; then I will take a cup or give a drink if possible, and the other end in the child's mouth, and I will lick it until the vapors come out of the child's mouth; then I will suckle it, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the second part is completed.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	When she remains after this treatment, and if it does not improve, then order the patient to massage their left hand with oil of sesamum or mustard seed oil, and then apply it to the affected area, and repeat as needed; when she finds it, press and stretch it slightly, so that the joint does not slip during extraction. However, it is necessary to move it lightly to the right and left, and then pull; if it comes and becomes red.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	If the mouth of the joint is squeezed, we have said that the treatment is to stretch and fumigation of herbs; and if it does not do all that we have said, then keep from pulling; but it may be that what is in the mouth of the joint, you tie it to the woman's breast, then cleanse it with four-drug ointment; if it comes back and returns, and it becomes stronger; but always, when it comes out, if it gives off a bad smell in the stomach and head, and stains the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	If it comes to that, then simple fumigations are in order: no one of the ancients has proven fumigations of cresson and dry figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument is made with it to fumigate the woman with the retention of flowers and the secondine if this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it seems like a dog, and one puts the subtle head on nature, and the large heads under the fire; and it is the fumigations with charcoal, and the smoke as much as it is greasy, and another one begins again.
de percier lou fondement	to perceive the foundation.
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who have not perceived the foundation, but they have felt a subtle smoke: if it comes to that, to do the ballet that he perceives that smoke at his turn, and does not perceive anything of spatumile agut, and keeps the plaster that it does not touch; then put on the soft one in wine and oil, then the care of the ointment as much as it is healthy.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not remain, if you put or prick a needle in it, and leave it hands free, and it is soon seen when the child looks up in the bedrooms.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And never comes this wound of the soil or abscess; if it comes, if you cure it, if as we have said, the needle.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula with great foundation.
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from the foundation are nodulous, and grow when they come out of the lower part, or in the space between them; and if this nodularity is old, it moves, and becomes moist or subtle, and never are these fistulas permanent; and they are known by the fact that they are caused by egestion or ventosity when the patient evacuates, and by chance some jump.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that reach the bladder, and almost the entire vagina; and they reach the joint of the cuxe, and the knee.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And if you cannot find the fistula at its base, and it does not have a base: and it is that you cut your index or base with an iron or steel needle in the fistula when it does not have bends.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if it has bends, then cut a small tent of plonc or horse hair, as you feel the tent or the hair in your hand; and if you do not feel it, and there is no outflow of egestion, wind, or ver, as we have said: be careful that it does not perforate; if you hurry to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	When the fistula is present in the bladder or urethra, and the urine suddenly comes out, and cannot be stopped by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is perceived at the joint of the thigh, if it is in the tense limb at the knee; if it is not a tortuosity and the invention of the pain enters, if it is that it is everted below the bowel, and there is no medicine to stop it by rubbing; and in these fistulas there is no cure except labor and vanity of the proud who get involved in them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In the one that is not a new and old fistula, with hope for health by iron, as I have experienced, and it is that the patient's pain comes between your hands on his back; and he helps his legs until they reach his thighs, and they are inclined to his belly; then bore a hole in the skin, or if it has tortuosity, as long as you watch or the tension comes.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels pain at the foundation, and if you reach the end of your index finger, it means that he is trying to hold on; and if you discover or feel between your thumb the scar or the char, then check if it is intact; if not, it cannot be cured.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	All kinds of wounds can be healed, but it's rare; and this help is what we do, if it is the subtle cauterization according to the size of the fistula, as said before; and the boute is put all inside the fistula as it comes out from the foundation; and do this twice or three times, as you check that these chars are firm, which look like a feather of oyster; then the cure of thin wounds is made, as they are, then the cure of ointment anointing char and soldering.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is in good health, so be it.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If the patient is not in good health, so be it. If he tries to enter, and does not penetrate the fundament, and enters the body and covers it with a thick blanket of char or smoke, you will see the fistula at this point where the covering ends; if the cope begins at the beginning of the fistula, and comes before the tent, and then cauterizes after, as long as it reaches the top of the tent; it will be delivered from the tent, and will hurt; then mold those charred parts that look like a feather’s tip, and there will be none left.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	If you lack it, and cut between you and the wound, whether by fire or medicinal heat.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cautery, there are two things to know: it is the surety of these burned bones, and the coagulation of blood and the closure of wounds; then the treatment of wounds with boiled or unboiled herbs, as long as the wound bleeds, and it is not in the burned part; then cure the wound of sore gums with dry char, and these are the dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	If it is restored, it is healthy and will not return again.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes suddenly with great pain, and is moved away from the heart, and the abdomen is swollen or painful, and it should be questioned.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tension, and enter II is the cloth or skin or charred, or it is near to pierce, if not had been that of a bride and hope, by the administration of one of the three ways: or you cauterize as we have said, or you cover it gently, or if you press if it has tents and cure as we have said; and do not let too much forward, that you do not cover the foundation which holds the tension, and take the excretions by the will of the patient; then the cure, as we have said; by chance if it is healthy, or you untangle that covering and the mundance then when it is covered by the foundation, or by needle or another instrument appointed; then make the charred part which is in the wound as you please; then study to restore the wound, and to prolong the fistula in the part defuers the foundation: if it is still a lighter thing for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And no time are fistulas made in this way: and when you reach the end of the fistula, it is either too costly or difficult to remove the skin over it, if you take a tent according to this form:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And if you cut it in half and remove the tent along the entire fistula as much as it is at the end:
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is perceived in the margin of the deep furrow, then remove the thread from that fistula as much as you reach the end; and cut off the tip of the thread, and assemble the two ends, and pull them apart, and leave one or two; and keep it tightened until the threads are no longer affected by the skin that is between them, and heal the wound as much as it is sore and sound.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, if you try in all ways that you can think of, it will not work too much.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not possible to make the closing too tight, and then the treatment, as we have said, until it is healthy.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the rough spiny thorn by which the fistula is made is long and trenched; and on the other hand, not, because of this, it does not pierce or it cannot pierce, as you see here:
des emorroydes	of the emorys.
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Gouttes are of two kinds: either they are like resin at the foundation, and have small and large grains, and are cut towards the center, and have one or more points, and are sharp at the foundation and at the head of the foundation; but those that are sharp have little moisture, and are cut with a little bit of turquoise or a little bit of acid, and have the color of coral; and the cure for those who have made them sharp at the foundation is that you command the midwife to let them run in chambers, as long as the foundations are hard, and appear the points; if you haste, and can hold them with your nails, or take them with your fingers, then cut into their roots; and if they cannot be held by their moisture, then bend them to the limb, or to cloth, or a piece of camomile; and draw them out of your two hands, then cut them, and powder some hot powders that are in the cauterization leau; or you can cauterize them as is said in the cauterization chapter, and cure others as much as they are healthy; and if the foundations cannot issue, then clysterize the midwife with clyster bitter and sharp, and wash what is at the foundation, so that it may issue openly; and if the midwife's mouth is not closed, then cut the midwife's nails, and if the points are sharp at the foundation, then the cure is light; and if you cut the points with your nails or fingers, then cure them as we have said, so that they may be healthy, and may not fear the incision by fire.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. If it comes to your mind that you want to cut the seam according to this way: take one thread, thrust it into an awl, and then draw the thread through and make the awl perceive the other part, and turn the two ends of the other two threads around the awl, and if they are wide; and then tighten the thread, then knot it, and draw out the awl, and do the same to all the others, and leave the surplusance of the thread on the sand; then put the foundation with a smooth, oiled or waxed drapement, and put it down, and command the patient to lie down; and then let it be as long as it is tight, and when it is cut, if the cure for ointment and other cures, so that it is healthy.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	The first sentence to translate is "dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement." The translation of this line is
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there are squeezing of feces in the intestines, and by constriction of nature, and when the disease is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it comes to the point of a spatula or your nail scratching the wound, which does not allow it to dry out; then treat it as much as possible, until it is soaked as much as it can, and if it cannot be soaked, then the scratching continues more forcefully than before, until it becomes clean, and is burned; then treat it as much as possible.
dou fremit	The first line of the text translates
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	The first line of the text translates to: "A fly is a small insect that should be removed from the body, and it cannot be felt; and no time does the person feel it, and it is felt as if the person is dying of fremit, and it comes throughout the body, and more in the hands than in any other part.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	The second line of the text translates to: "And if you take a pin from a goose feather, or a vulture feather, and place it on the fremit, as long as the purple circle encircles the fremit entirely; then turn your hand over all the pin until you cover the entire fremit and remove it, and pull out the fremit at its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see that I make this tool of a copper or iron needle according to this form, and it is subtle and translucent:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	If you see that the cauterization does not move, if it is in front or in the chapter of cauterization.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of a circle.
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Never has a silver or archaut cauterization been made, nor an alloyed or hammered brass one; and never has any of these sharp and large ones, according to which they are used, been made.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Therefore, those that are used in the treatment of children and the weak and painful ones are sharp.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the clitoris is small and large if it is wide, or the belly is shaped like this:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And if it has a descent or the belly is likewise shaped, as you see, and the clitoris is perceived; and it has one of the coste's pertus, and the other I; and it is the belly or puts medicines from a beast's vessel or a pouch, and all around each pertus is perceived, and between each pertus I must do a stitch, then bore in these pertus I fasten the thread as tight as possible, then assemble the belly like a swine; and when the medicine is given, if the instrument has a thread before, then castrate; and this is the form of a circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	1. And let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and anoint the head with oil or unguent of urine or something similar, then lightly apply it; then the surgeon should carefully minister to his two hands together, as much as he can, then remove the plaster, and gently lift the patient's legs to the edge, and if the medicine seems to be working, so much as it can; and if the patient sleeps a whole night, it will be more help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	2. And if you have dislocated the hip due to disease of the abdominal muscles, and the medicine is not working, then it may recur when it is healthy.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	When the swelling or abscess is large or painful, if it is the same as that of a child; and this is the form of the subtle abscess when the skin is pulled:
des plaies	wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have said the treatment of wounds in the division; and you will say the treatments for hands and medicine, according to their completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are made, and according to the instrument or means by which they are made, and of how they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by cutting with a blade, or lance, or spear, or needle, or similar instruments; or according to the parts of the body, if it is the same as that of the neck, or chest, or belly, or liver, or stomach, and similar members; and I will tell you the treatment for each wound, and I will mention simple wounds on the neck, because the reminder will be in your chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes or breaks the bone, and the bone is not broken, if it is due to the griping of the wound or similar things, and the skin is completely torn and the wound is large, and you slightly doubt the occurrence of hemorrhage: if the head itself becomes healthier, and there is little blood from the wound, and it is healthier on the opposite side; and avoid the surgeon's fullness with wine and fatty foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not become healthier, if the meat is anemic and does not drink wine and does not eat fat, and applies to the wound, if there is a post-incision scar, it is oiled with oil of rose or only wine steeped; and if it does not post-incision scar, if it is applied to the wound, it is fresh at all its sanc, and it is not moved by the air, powder, which I will say a little later; and if it has been moved, if it applies some ointments, as long as it is healthy.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	When the wound is large, like that of a spearhead and its surroundings, and the lips cannot be reassembled by stitches, if they can be reassembled by sewing, if I may say so, as belly wounds, by sewing.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to bone, and can be held, and only by a nail; then treat the wound with medicine, and restore the hardness of the leather in the leg, and instruct the patient to eat large meats, such as testes and cooked flour, as well as chicken and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	If you have a wound or scar, and it does not reach the bone, and it is covered with skin, and it grows, then treat it; and if arteries are in the wound or vein, which cannot be stopped by medicines, if you want to stop the artery, and if you remove it slowly, if it is held by a thread; and if it does not benefit, if it is cauterized.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the cure is light: and that is to put on this powder which is always dry when the hand has touched it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of the powder is: take some incense, a part; sulfur three parts, and live chalz, and the subtle powder, and apply to the wound, and draw it out as much as it adheres to all its sand; and then put it well, and leave it to drip if it does not thicken, for one does not use the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never has it been done with only chalz, when one does not have incense or the sand of dragon, but that the hand has not touched the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is not healing, do the same here immediately; but use this powder instead; but use some digested ointments or flour of wheat made with vinegar and honey, as it grows bowed; then continue the care for other wounds until they are healthy.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the bone fracture comes with the wound, and it is small, if it is pulled out with fine tweezers; and I will tell you about this later in the bone fractures.
de la plaie dou col	of the severe wound
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound comes of the collar or it is simple, if there is no difference between it and the severe wound, but if the collar or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is a nerve, and there is no other remedy than leaving the treatment alone and not restricting anything, as nerves pull back; and nothing should be put on the wound, as the substance of the nerves is cold, and continuation with it is with the brain, which is the colder part of the body; but let the medicine be, if like cold water is washed in gentle dew, and mixed with olive oil, and the wound is washed again in gentle dew, and other parts of the body similarly treated, and moistened.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, and it is full of knots, then the cure as soon as it is healthy.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	The patient's wounds are clean and filled with blood, if the point is lower on the body; and if the artery is cut, and the blood flows from the wound, if it is stopped, and the gauze, and the cauterization is done properly; and if the spine of the neck is cut, or the jaw, and the mandible is held in place, as long as the meat does not touch the jaw bone, and then the wound is dressed according to its natural shape; and then the bandage is removed, and some gaps are left, and the treatment of the swelling is continued until it is healed; and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, if the patient wishes; and if there are pieces of bone, if they are carefully removed, and those that cannot be removed, if they are left as much as possible to allow the wound to heal and become less inflamed and infected; and if the wound is fresh, if powder is applied on top of the powder I have mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	If it has in the wound bone and if it has an abscess, then the treatment is as I have said in my chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound of the arrow or the spear
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is of the wound of the arrow or the spear, and the wound is gushing blood, then look at whether the wound is mortal; and if it is not gushing blood, and it is fresh all around the bone, then do not delay in applying powder to the wound at the first hour, nor let it dry, and wrap it with cloth; but if you do not have powder, then apply wet cotton to the wound for soothing the moisture, and make the patient lie on the wound three or four or more hours, unless spasms or tremors of the chest occur from the wound; and when you see the bones in proper position, know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Treat the wounds and other wounds as necessary; if it cannot be cured, and it causes pain, perform incisions as the patient has made them; according to what is needed.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	If the wound is an incision or a cut, and it is simple, on the front or back, if the treatment is by the one in front; if it is large, with poultice; if it is small, with powder, and if it pierces the bone and breaks into pieces, if the wound wants to be treated, and if they are not broken, if they are left exposed, if other wounds have been extracted; and other wounds on other parts are judged as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	The first sentence to translate is "dou derrompement dou ventre". The translation of
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The first sentence to translate is "dou derrompement dou ventre". The translation of "dou derrompement dou ventre" is "great abdominal pain". This phrase is a medical term used to describe a significant amount of pain in the abdomen. The pain can be caused by various factors such as inflammation, infection, or other medical conditions. In the given context, it seems that the text is discussing the treatment and management of such pain.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and there is no injury to the intestines, and it is difficult to dress, this is done by one of the two methods: either because of the size of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is twisted due to the blow.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is twisted, you should treat it in this way: soften a sponge or a piece of cloth only with water, or soak it in hot water and let it dry, and pull the intestine as much as it needs to unwind; and never forget to do this while it is still tight, and it will become loose.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	When you see the flame departing, if the intestine is rough or sharp and uneven, it is because of this that the entrance is narrow; and if it cannot enter, then a small wound is made with the instrument on the point of the bone, and the excess tissue is cut off; and the first cure is to trim it, that no one should be cut without great necessity or not; and this is the stitches for the wound: if it does not tear through the skin and does not close, and then it looks like this.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	When the wound is enlarged, and the intestine jumps out, if you reset it according to its natural form in its own place, then you will have done well, because this is the best.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is wide, and it is in the lower abdomen, if you can make the patient lie on his back and raise his legs higher than his chest; and if it is in the lower abdomen, then he should place his chest and pelvis higher than the parts below, and thus the wound in the one of the two parts should be higher than the other; and it is necessary to manage this in large and dirty wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	When the wound is small, and it is in the lower abdomen, if you can make the patient lie on his back and raise his legs higher than his chest; and if it is in the lower abdomen, then he should place his chest and pelvis higher than the parts below, and thus the wound in the one of the two parts should be higher than the other; and it is necessary to manage this in large and dirty wounds. If the wound is small, and you can make the patient lie on his back and raise his legs higher than his chest, then you should place your hand on the wound and assemble the lips; and this is the common way of stitching, and it is that you prick an awl or more, according to the size of the wound, then leave the head of the wound and insert an awl or a strong thread; and perforate the skin with the skin awl, which is the skin of the thigh, as far as you can perforate this part, and assemble the four corners of the skin with the four corners of the thread; then pull the thread through the hole you have made with the first awl, and then assemble the four corners of the skin with the thread you have just used, and continue to do so until all the wound is closed; and the threads should be fine and not too thick, because fine threads penetrate the entire flesh, and too thick ones do not enter well; therefore they should be fine; and do not insert the threads too close to the wound and the skin, so that they do not open the wound when the patient sleeps, and then cover or wrap the threads with cloth or blankets at the points where the threads are inserted, and leave them as long as the wound is open; and this way of stitching with threads is more convenient in small wounds, because it is easier to prick with the second stitch, and it is that you assemble the four corners of the skin and the four corners of the blanket with a fine thread; when you have perforated the four corners of the skin where you started, then pull the thread through the hole you have made with the first awl, and then insert the thread between the four corners of the stitch, in the same way as you did with the threads; and then cover or wrap the threads with cloth or blankets at the points where the threads are inserted, and this stitching sews the wound, and I saw a wound that one had, which was in the belly, and it was of a coat, and it was more than a palm in width, and it had intestines that were more than a palm in width, and it was the wound in the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I returned to the intestine and after it had been 24 hours, it was 15 years old, and the wound was healed, and I cured it, and it became healthy.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the patient told me that he would die, and this was a miracle; and I did not cure him with medicines, because there were no medicines in my league, nor in any other place; and I washed the wound twice a day with honey water, and when it was healthy, I stopped.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or you will tell me the two main methods of sewing: take the needle, and cut off the end of the thread that is closest to the eye; when it has perforated the right way through the whole, if the handle or the tip of the needle is larger than the thread, or if you have cut off the thread too short, then make another piercing from the other part of the denuded part; and the stitches will be seen if you do it like the barber does the beard, and leave once the wax from one side, and take it back again on the other, until the stitching is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of stitching, as Galen describes it, is what everyone does, which naturally brings together the two parts, and applies one end of the thread to the other, in this way: first, make a loop or thread end near by, and then perceive that one, and leave the other thread ends; then turn the loop, and perceive it at the part nearest to the center of the wound, as the other thread ends; then perceive the other part at the center of the wound, using other thread ends on either side; and this is the most common method of stitching.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	1. If the patient hears this speech and no one testifies, it is necessary to sew the belly to the eyes, or tie them together; and it must be done by sewing one eye from one side, and the other from the other side, in the manner of those who are crooked; and afterwards, if the rupture is in the belly, it is the belly that is more painful than the other bellies.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	1. The judgment of the wound is if it is similar to the judgment of other wounds: and that if you treat the fresh wound with all its blood, unless it has moved, then you must reinsert the intestine and the gut; then put some powdered charcoal on the wound, and if it has moved, then put any ointment that is present, as long as the wound bows; then close the wound, and make sure it is safe, and watch it; then treat the wound as you would with other wounds, as long as it is healthy; and if you have no medicine, then put some, as soon as it comes out to gush blood, cotton wool, and rub it twice the morning until it is healthy.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis. de fistule ou qu’ele soit	Of a fistula or if it is

Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	1. If the patient has a fiancé whose hair is turning gray and the corruption is not yet advanced, and the hair is thick and the smell is unpleasant, then the treatment is to apply Egyptian medicine: observe if the breasts are large and the odor is unpleasant, then take ointment, oil, and lotion, and apply it to the wound at the fire for as long as the medicine turns red and becomes as thick as honey; then take according to your need, and make it in wine and honey, and apply it to the breasts and stop the discharge; let the medicine remain for two hours, then withdraw it by straining; repeat this process as long as the breasts become deformed and the pain subsides, and never use smoke from grapevine wood and water, but only honey and wine, which have the property of cleansing and washing; if the patient cannot bear the smoke, or the medicine does not cure the wound with smoke, then apply the medicine with oil and wine; or apply it with other medicines and ointments, as I have mentioned their properties and uses; if the discharge from the nipple is small and the ointment cannot enter, then make a pouch of Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment and apply it to the wound; if the wound is too large, so that the leu or the clistere can only enter a little, and the discharge from the nipple is large, so that the cope or the lower part of the leu is not enough, then apply the medicine.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement. de l’aposteme de l’ungle	Of the abscess of the finger
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Gangrene is a grievous wound that affects the finger, either the little or ring finger, or sometimes other parts; and when it becomes infected, if it is not cared for, it causes the gangrene to spread rapidly, and reaches the bone as far as the root of the finger, and may even reach the bone, and then the flesh becomes black and putrid, causing great pain.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and your cure does not help, then you should cut away all the excess of the finger, and then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The fire cautery is a great help when the bone is healthy, and the nail is healthy; and if the nail presses on the skin, and it begins to prick, and burn, then you should remove the part of the nail that points at the skin, and cut it off high, and cover it with a layer of skin subtly and lightly, and put on the remaining part of the nail medicated and corrosive ointment to heal all; then the treatment of wounds as long as they are healthy.

And if the corrosion is in the bone, if it presses, and flows, because as much as the bone corrupts and is, so it cannot be healed; and if you see the other corroding, if you cut it in the way said before, then treat it as long as it is healthy; and if it is hard, and cut off, and it feels great pain, then it must be treated first; then cover the nail with a layer of wet clay when cutting across the skin, and make sure that the part that was cut does not reach the bone that is far from the nail, because the patient will feel too much pain; and if this happens, then put something on it to soothe.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain of the elbow
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The elbow dislocation that occurs in the hands of some men by chance is very common, and often it does not cause any pain, and never causes damage, and no one is born with this in the root of the jointure, or the birth is in no one's two.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile. Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The causes that come to us come either at birth, or from wounds, or from burns, or from similar things.

des vils	of warts
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Warts are large, hanging in folds of melancholic fullness, which come in more and more members of the chest; and more often in the legs of those who go to prayer and work and carry, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, it is necessary that you never administer any purging of colic, and then the proper treatment of the basin.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The treatment of iron is according to two methods: one is on the warts, and it draws out the black blood; and the other method is that you let the vein flow, and it drains all.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	1. The size of the wound is as follows: first, apply hot oil to the leg, as much as possible, then tightly wrap it with linen from the groin to the part below the knee; then cut and tie the vein in one, two, or three places, with a wide opening, then remove and let the black blood flow into your hand, from one to the other, as much as the patient's strength allows; then sew it up, and command that it be stitched with black meat threads; and continue the evacuation and cleaning of the wounds as the veins become flat, and do not leave any loose threads.

de la voinne civile	of the civil vein

This vein is located in the legs, in hot parts where there are no herbs or trees, and in the earth where there is no moisture; and by chance it may be located elsewhere than in the legs, and this is the cause that comes from the skin, as the snake's core comes out and goes, it is located between the hide and the cartilage.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.
