Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And never once in this vein do the hands fail, and at the same time when it opens at the joint of the thumb, or the thumb, and a drop of blood comes out, and it suddenly falls; cure the patient if we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Of those that are born between leather and char
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our country "beef disease," because it often occurs in cows, and is a small worm that goes between leather and char, and goes up and down the whole body, and is felt very well in the limbs as soon as it comes out of the hide or when it wants to, and is caused by the food of some humors, such as serpents, snakes, and worms, and ascarides or the belly; and one doubts its malice, because when it goes through the body, it goes to the head, and comes to the oil, by chance it returns, and destroys the oil; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see the wound healing and drying, if it cannot be otherwise than when it will: if it comes to pass that you read the leg and the bone from a strong limb well closed, then cut it off and take it out, and put it in a vessel in the char, and do not touch it, if it is cauterized with fire as it dies; and the greatest harm it can do, if it comes to pass that it touches the oil, as we have said; and if you see it coming near the oil, if it strains the hair around it, then cut it off, and take it out; and it is necessary to use the mule with disinfection of solutions of medicines for the humors of men, and avoid foods that are harmful to the body.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	The pain that comes from dislocation
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called "waxing" in our land, and is a pain that comes to any part of the body, and spreads from one part to another; and I see what I have told you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called a female patient, and I saw my arm, and I saw a small bump in the vein of my shoulder; and afterwards, I saw it growing as if it were a stone in the shoulder, faster than anything else, as if silver were being cut from the bone; the pain left that arm and moved to the shoulder, and became twisted in the shoulder, and then a little later spread throughout the body, until it came to the other shoulder; then I was told that it was dislocating again, as I see.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was amazed to see how it moved from limb to limb, as I had never wanted this disease to happen in this way.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	Indeed, I wanted to make sure that the limbs moved well and did not cause pain in the joint, but I did not want it to be so. I thought it was because the woman had tightened her corset, discovered the veins, and because of this appeared the constraint; but I did not know if this was true for those who are delicate, who have moist veins and responding veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see the curing of this disease, and the patient feels pain, does it open as we have said, if the limb is tightened and then released, and then held as long as the constraint at the knee persists; and cauterize the knee; and if you do not see it with your eyes, if the cure of those who cause the constraint, if like pus pills, and serapem pills, and similar things.
des saiettes	The first sentence to translate is: "Ou c
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the wounds they cause.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of arrows includes those with large points, small points, and barbs; those with sharp angles, curved points, and hooks; those that pierce any part of the body in different ways: either by the head, chest, liver, spleen, intestines, bladder, uterus, and other organs. Some arrows also have barbs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	If it appears that you are dying from the extraction of this arrow, as the death will come later in other ways; and if the sign does not appear immediately, and the arrow is not visible, then the wound is deep and requires further treatment, such as amputation and wound care.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	When the shoulder joint is dislocated and the bone pierces the bone, and the head of the cervix is forced against the eye, it is when there is scotomie, sode, esvertin, and roujor of the eyes, and inflammation and roujor of the tongue, and spasme and permixtion of understanding, and vomiting of cole; and by chance it is without nose or ears; and by chance it affects the word and voice; and a jump of the white, moist wound, resembling poulz, and like a gout of char, and if this sign appears, if you hold to the cure, and remove the arrow if it is not in.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of the shoulder when it is cut or bruised is that it pains or aches, and it feels as if it is becoming hard, without voiding; and by chance the shoulder becomes still like the thigh, and in a short time black blood comes out, and there is cold and cold frost, and sinking: then the signs of death begin to appear.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arm that is not moving is that there are no signs of swelling from the wound, and the throat is engorged, and the face turns pale, and it sighs high and cries out in pain.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	1. If the arrowhead is found in the covering of the chest, if it hits the small ribs; and it causes great pain and suffering; and all the members of the shoulder are moved.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	2. If the arrowhead is found in the stomach by chance, if it jumps from the wound, nothing undigested from the meat.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	3. If the arrowhead is found in the stomach and jumps through the intestine at once, if there is no hope in the treatment, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	4. If the arrowhead is found in the bladder and the urine jumps suddenly and comes out, and the patient feels great pain: the wound is deadly.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other member, if the face and neck and shoulder and arm and spine and back and ribs and sides and legs, are safe according to other dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the louse or artery, and it is not removed, as I will tell you if I remember, because you are doing it yourself.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to my home one arrow that cut through the root of the nose: I tried to remove it, and it came out from another part of the grease of the ear, and it was safe without any pain.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And I took out one arrow that was in the grease of the oil outside the paper, and the arrow was safe, and it could not reach any further than the point towards the opposite side, and it was as big as a Turkish arrow, for all it was light on the ears; the wound was safe, and I did not have any accidents.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And there was a gash in the throat of a man, and it was the Arab gash at the ears: I was the beard, and subtle as I passed, and it was healthy for the Crestians.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And there was a gash in the body of a man, which I thought was fatal or from the stomach, and then after 30 days, if it did not change its position; I opened the gash, sewed it up, and it healed, and there was no accident.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if a man has a gash in the side or back, and it is sutured; and the wound heals, and does not change its natural positions, and does not find any harm in any of its natural works.

And see if another man, who cuts a wound in his face, and feels the pain; and delays for some time to suffer great pain; and then other similar things.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And a wound was found on the face of the king, who was cut by a nail in the left part; and it was a deep wound; and it was all sewn up. I was called to the care after three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If I found the wound to be very tight.

Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought that this was the tip of the shoulder I placed my hand on the uneven joint, because the shoulder did not swell; and I seemed to feel the dislocation.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I placed my hand on the uneven joint, and relieved the pain on the right side, and held for a long time until the patient felt the dislocation in his knee; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I placed my hand on the uneven joint, and relieved the pain with medicine that was corrosive to the skin, until it was over, and I felt the end of the shoulder that was sticking out of the knee; then I put the end of the plague in the same place with the medicine, as soon as the patient's shoulder became visible; and it healed well in four months, and then I removed the needles and the threads on both sides, and could not stop; therefore, I continued to refine and invent ways to strangle, as soon as I had made the needles well, according to how the form will come at the end of this chapter, as soon as I see it, and restore the plague.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	The patient thinks that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored: I will restore it therefore, and the wound was sore, and the health of the patient was completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	I did not say the quality of extracting some arrows, if you put your care only on what I do not tell you, because the books cannot make everything look good; but the masters of the art can make good things out of poor ones, and of what is present and deficient, they use nine or ten operations and nine instruments, as the things drawn down in this art come out badly.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not come from the limbs or they are made of hair according to two ways: either by the hand or they enter, or by another part; and the one that is thrown by the hand or it enters, is an arrow that enters in the flesh, and it has never been thrown once.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	If she does not jump now, if the pain is so great that the bones are exposed and the issue is delayed, and then she becomes fixed in the bone, and she cannot move if any joints are left, and each joint is tightened; therefore she jumps, and if she does not jump, if the pain is so great that it pierces through all parts of the body subtly, as long as the bones are exposed, then the issue will be delayed and the limb will be fixed.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	If the arrowhead becomes fixed in the bone and is wedged into one of the lobes of the liver or any other accidents I have mentioned to the surgeon: if he does not remove it, but leaves it as long as it remains even after some time, because the arrowhead becomes wedged in the liver, it is a matter of life and death.

And if the dislocation is severe and cannot be reduced, then the patient should immediately seek medical attention as I have advised; then treat the limb until it is healthy.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the dislocation is not visible in the limb and cannot be felt, then the patient should try to locate it using any available instruments; and if you feel it, if there is no blood loss or nerve damage, then treat the wound as much as the pain allows; and cut or crush the ears of the limb as much as possible, until you can amputate it; and be careful not to cause unnecessary pain.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	If you do not once, if the bone until it is read in order to be torn, then it will be pulled out, because the extraction is painful.

If the dislocation of the bone causes it to move in the opposite direction, if you do not follow what we have said in this chapter; and you should be made an incision on the nerve and vein, and make an opening according to how you think you can remove the arrow while being careful, or quickly, or firmly, or gently; and make the patient according to the shape of the bone as it was when the arrow hit it, because this is the greatest help that can be given, and if you do not, if they make it according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The first line of the text translates to: "The arrow that comes from another part, or it opens no thing of him, or his skin is shrunk in some place where one can see or feel it: then remove it, as much as the barbs can take, and then extract it: if it jumps now.

des voinnes dou cors communes	Common veins of large size:
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	The veins that are safe to cut include the 31st, of which the head is the 16th, which is to say: the two branches that are after the ears, which are called the "herbage" arteries; and the two arteries that are in the two temples appearing; and the veins that are in the two eyes, which are called the "aspires"; and the vein that is cut at the front; and the vein that is at the top of the nose; and the girdles that are on the collar; and the veins that are in the lips of the mouth, and these are the veins that are called the "augeherich"; and the veins that are at the bottom of the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	1. The veins that are commonly found in the arm are V in each arm: one is the cranial, and it is on the western costal side, and it is called the "giant's vein" or "vain of the head"; and the femoral is called the "fasten", and it is composed of the cranial and the basilic, and they are called the "giant's vein of the chest"; and the basilic is on the eastern costal side, and it is called the "giant's abdomen", and it is below the femoral, and it is the one that is found, which opens manifestly into the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	The safeguard is the vein that lies between the ear and the anus, and if it swells; and in the leg, there are three veins: one is the corbicle of the left shoulder, which is the small intestine on the left side of the chest; the second one is called "nisse," which is at the right shin; and in the other leg, there are three veins similar to these.

The benefit of the veins after the ears is that it helps with catheters and drainage; and the quality of the vein, as I tell you, and it is that you cleanse the patient's leg or the veins are of a rough cloth; then strain the patient's hand over a vessel, as long as the veins appear behind the ears in the dependent part of the chest: take the lancet, and cut through the vein just above the bone, then gently hold your hand on all the veins until you cop and the leather and the vein well through, and make the suction as long as you see; then let it go and hold it until it is healed, as you see; and I have already said the incision and the cauterization of the first book.

de la sainie des leivres	Of the health of the deer
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The health of the lips of the deer is helped in closing the mouth, and preventing decay of the gums, and cracks in the lips, and sores and infections.

And the quality of the health is to make the patient stand before you, and pull their collar as I have said; then turn the lip, and look at the eyes, of which one is on the left side and the other on the right, and they are black, and have dark-colored teeth: therefore, treat both, and if you do not know them, and you are in doubt, then the largest of each part, and so do the eyes that are inside and outside, for it is a similar manner.

It is necessary for the one who is in pain and forceful, and has skill in extracting poison, to make a larger wound, and have wide flames; and for the weak one, the opposite, and it is healthier and more often successful, and it should be made healthier by cutting across, not by pinching; and this method of healing is saved from the dislocation of poison and the weakness of nerves, and it is worth that the long wound is not wide.

Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is filled with blood, if it is left without being strained and as long as the abscess is not relieved.

des sainies de ventouse	Of the wounds of childbirth
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Ventouses are made of horn, or iron, or glass; and ventilation is done in two ways: either by cutting and drawing out blood, or by cutting.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this ventilation, which is made by cutting and drawing out blood, is done in two ways: either it is all on fire, or hot; and ventilation which is made by cutting and extracting blood is made in fourteen days of the course of the corps, of which some are all in one part, and the others in another part, and the others in the costeis of the collar; the ventilation of the chief is made at the menton; the ventilation of the shoulders is made at the elbows; the ventilation of the crupies is made at the wrists; the ventilation of the arms is made at the shoulders; the ventilation of the legs is made at the knees; the ventilation of the ankles is made at the feet; and the ventilation does not touch any veins, only small ones that are scattered in the course of the body, and therefore it does not cause any harm to anyone, as we do with wounds; and it is necessary that it be dressed, and neither hot nor cold, in no disease that comes from repletion, as long as the corps is vuidiez.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	1. If necessary, due to illness or habit, if the patient coughs once in the beginning of the month, or at the end, and more often in each ten days; for there are those who, when they cough, have a heavy chest; and if such people have fullness and redness in their face, and in their chest, and at the collarbone, and have dark spots; and those who have a chill in their stomach, and lose their tongue, and vomit blood; and if there are those who sneeze, and see red blood, and white blood, and death, and similar things.

Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The health of the head helps in relieving the pain, and it is only after all the blood has been evacuated that this fasting is allowed; and this fasting should be done under the supervision of the physician or midwife, as it can cause great harm to those who have cold complexions or are pregnant, because this can lead to serious complications. For this reason, only those who have cold diseases should fast.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often heal, if they become incapacitated, and therefore it is necessary to put the gauze a little further down due to the fear of incapacity.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The collar is placed on the neck of the shoulder and the head, and for this reason it is useful in the treatment of the chest, and to remove the catheter, and for all, and to relieve; and it is necessary to put it on a little loosely, because if it is too tight, it can cause incapacity or stomach or liver.

Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	1.
