Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the vacuum administered by fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And it has two wide and half palm-sized parfois, and it has one cost or edge around the little puncture I, so as to bind a needle, and it is of iron or steel, in front so that it does not bend the patient's arm at the time of putting it on the limb; and in the mileau there is a hole of iron or steel for a screw to be inserted, and it is either large or small according to the disease and the age of those who take them; for the vacuums of children are different from vials, and thin than fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	1. And it must be put on the dressing over the member: take the wax candle or liniment, and insert it into the hole of the dressing that is in the hole of the wax candle, so that it shines at the end of the dressing that it does not burn the patient; then put it over the member, and you must be as tight as we have said, if you see that it rises, and then remove the dressing; and take the liniment as before, and repeat it often, if you can.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	2. In the dressing that is used when the patient is ill with catarrh, there is no hole or percussion, and it is not used unless it is flat with a cold, and is put over the member only when it is flat with a cold; and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	1. Withouts are not plucked except in members where it is impossible to put on stockings due to their smallness, such as the lips and genitals, and similar parts; and in these parts, if they are without withouts of char, like does or neis, and others like this; and the quality of the user is that when you find withouts which are in soft waters, if you take them; you put them in a soft water bath, as long as they are not pregnant, and have nothing in the belly; then it is healthy for the vein and the wind, then clean the member as much as it is red, and put on the withouts; and when they are flat and smooth, if it is possible to put on a wind, it is put on, because this is after.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	1. If not, then lift the leg of silk, and then the hot one, well, and then the stretch it; and if the wound is too large after the corset of the bones, then soak a piece of linen in cold water, and put it on, as long as the bones are not swollen; and if the bones swell, then put on vitriol or gas, or similar things, as long as they are swollen; or put on half of the legs of grapes, and leave them as they burn on the leg, if it now sticks; and if you have more of this, then take other bones.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the wounds do not take on their medicine, then frothe the league of the salve as much as it will, and then put it on, and as soon as they feel the soothing, if they do not heat up; and when you see that they are taking in the powder and the flax or the hemp, or the cinder, if they start to burn now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This begins the book of wounds
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	These cauteries are often necessary in the art of medicine, and they are both a treatment for wounds and a way to dislocate bones.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Tell me, dear friend, what you think of this cauterization, that the folk do not see it as a way to treat wounds, and that they have never seen any ancient books or letters on the subject; and for this reason, science has been neglected in our land, because I have never found any book on the subject, and neither have you, except perhaps through the science of ancient books, or by my own study and treatment of the subject, by experiment, and by habit of my life; and I have described in this cauterization what is contained in it, and summarized it at the end, and shown clearly the forms of the dislocations that are made, as I have done in these two previous chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say at the beginning of this book the sum of words and chapters or sentences, and moreover, to prove it, if those who have experienced it believe and learn this noble art, and they teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when a fracture, dislocation, torsion, or twisting occurs in any part of the body, if you do not treat the wounded man on both sides, nothing will help, as weakness of the heart, or childbirth, or wounds; or if you hold him tightly, it is not very tight, or too loose; and if the wound is cold, it is to know that the drinks are cold, and do not drink beer, nor eat thin grasses, and do not fill your belly with too much meat that fills the veins with blood, as long as you have no doubt of apoplexy or expansion of matter in the member; if the wounded man regains consciousness after being under the influence of the drug he has used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	When the bones begin to heal, if it is necessary to remove the patient's flesh that causes great swelling, or if there is viscosity, like wheat cooked in vinegar, and tests, and pies, and sausages, and meat of goats, and fish, and large wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For the healing of swelling is reduced and the fracture is healed as quickly as possible.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And you advise that fractures of bones and deformities cannot be well recovered or mended according to their nature by the care of the limbs, but rather those that are too flexible, like those of small children; but if it is necessary to cut into the bone and large tendons that are torn and joined together, as much as possible, and not to cut too deep, and for this reason it is necessary to remove large pieces of flesh, like we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And you know that there are many ways to cut.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the cutting of the head is different from that of the foot or leg, and I will tell you all the ways of cutting in this chapter.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a cut that goes through and another that just pricks, like the width of a quill to write.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if it is a cut with a wound, and a cut is just a small gash.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each cut has its own engine and its own instrument in restoration, according to what remembers come to his head; and it is the fracture of the bone by which the tooth is torn, and opened well by defense, and some pressure of the hand; and when it is not tortuosity or incision, but the pain is great, and the patient does not have a fracture, it may be tortuosity, or gash, or small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If you cannot move it with your hand alone, but use the medicines that will come later, and then gently pull it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And examine the fracture that will occur in the fall, and the two parts that are disjointed, it is now appropriate to gently place them back together, unless the wound opens and bleeds; and if the wound opens and comes, as long as there is no pain, until the wound is calmed, then it should be placed gently and wisely at the point where you can easily and carefully, and consider that the restoration of the part is lighter than the restorations of other parts or pieces; then gently pull, as it will come later.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	1. And if in the bone of the foot, if it is broken into two parts, if it is hands or arm, or a part of your arm, or a cord, or a cord and your hand; and put the member according to its natural figure, so that when the broken parts of the member are evened out, if you reset by your hands the additions in their places in the muscles that you push, and keep that by your effort does not cause further injury or pain; and adjust well the two heads of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	2. And it feels good in your hand if it seems that it is not well: if it curves beautifully, and is not strained too much, do not press as they who come by their effort cause the aposteme chaut and contraction of the member, as we have wanted many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	When the member is at rest, if the patient carefully guides the helper so that it does not move, neither by watching nor sleeping nor turning, nor in any other way; and ensure that the member is firmly held so that it does not feel any pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when it does not feel pain, if it is not yet at rest, and it is necessary to put the member in order so that it does not feel any pain; and keep it steady so that it remains in its place, so that twisting does not occur when it is restored; and the quality of the broken member is according to what I am saying.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	It is known that the broken member has different sizes in smallness, breadth, and shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For the patient has many limbs, as if they were threads and similar things: if it comes to wrapping them with linen and similar materials; and those that are large, like a thick rope and leg: if it comes to wrapping them with a wide and hard rope, because the large ones tighten all the large member, and draw it evenly, unless it has no knot; then it is lightly wrapped with light bands, three or four times according to the member, and the hand is tightly tied around all the member, then go to the end of the fracture and draw it less than the fracture itself; and soften the member a little and a little, as you please to give a large part of the healthy part of the leg, then take another member, and turn the wrist towards the broken part of the leg; then return to the part opposite the fracture, and draw it gently, not too much nor too little, as we have said in the first step of the fracture; then put between the wrapped limbs of linen or silk, as they are equal, and then put all the stitches well made, if it has no gape or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	If it is inflamed or infected, apply something soothing to the inflammation, such as a poultice of oats, or a piece of cloth soaked in vinegar, or a poultice of palm leaves, and make sure they are according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	However, it is necessary that the dressing placed on the wound be larger and broader than the others; and also longer if it is for a small or large member; then tighten the bandage as you did in the first case, then tie a string around it, as you did in the first case, but do not make it too tight; and the string must be clean, neither too thick nor too thin, and should be of linen; for if the string is too thick, like the works of the fools who make their laces of linen thread, it can cause harm, because the wound cannot be held even if it is too fine, and only one can be obtained between each stitch.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is examined by the hands of the maledictions after they are cleansed with water, if they make holes in the linen or lace, if it does not cleave.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the splinter, and the horn is broken, I will tell you the cure for this after.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And I advise you that it is not easy to straighten all the broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limbs are large, it is not possible to put the splints on immediately after birth or within seven days, according to your aposteme's experience; and here is the way the ancient emplaustres were used to restore fractures, dislocations, and torsion: and that you take flour which is between the miller's millstones, and mix it with a lot of urine, and make this mixture, neither too thin nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common way to restore fractures in more ways, and even in women and children, because it is neither too harsh nor too harsh.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Other methods for repairing breaks and dislocations and twists: take barley and linen and glue and Arabian gum and ginger, and rosemary; mix with aloes, and alechil; and make a powder, and mix with honey; if the complexion of the face is hot, use this plaster as it is well-composed, and restores broken bones quickly, and benefits many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Other methods for plasters that benefit twists: take Arabian gum and vinegar, and rosemary; mix with aloes, and alechil; acetic acid (vinegar), and cook well, and administer with honey or honey and milk.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Other methods of splinting include joints and bones, which help alleviate the pain resulting from their dislocation, and the breakage: take fresh leaves, and mix them with oil and warm butter, and place them on the limb.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These plasters do not repair, but they are beneficial for alleviating inflammation and directly reducing bone pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of splinting that repairs broken bones: take dry fig leaves and earth oak leaves, and bind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method of splinting for repairing bone fractures and reducing inflammation.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	1. Take the root of malva, chamomile, violet flowers, flour of violets, and each part in equal amounts; and boil, and distill with wine, and wash the limbs with moist urine, or with fresh urine, and use.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	2. Another method for healing more quickly than the first is when the abscess is severe and comes to restore the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	3. Take the roots of malva, and linseed meal, balsam, honey, and salt, and each part in equal amounts; and boil, and distill with salty or sweet urine, or with wine, according to the choler of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	In the book of Ypocras, it is stated that no material is used to set a broken bone for restoration, and nothing else, and he said that it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	It seems that Galen suggests that when setting a broken bone for restoration, one should use dry, hot things, such as mustard and aloes, and incense, and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to alleviate pain and injury: take mugath and chevolz of ox hooves, or the feet of oxen, and vismalve, and seil igalment, and the boils, and make an application and put it on the affected part.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then a little later, and take care that the patient does not feel any pain in his shoulder joint, or stiffness, if it does not come from the hands; if it comes from the shoulder, whether it is painful or prickly, itching or swelling, if you hurry, and remove it, and now apply the plaster; take a light cloth, moisten it with seawater, dip in cold water, and raise the limb as much as the prickle stops, and soothe the pain; then let the member rest for an hour, then put on a dry cloth, smooth with cold or rose oil, and tie with a thread, as long as you are sure not to have fever; and let the inflammation in the member subside, and soothe the pain, then resume the gentle application, a little plaster, and do not strain it too much; and gradually as it gets better.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the wound is raw and bleeding and painful and swollen, and you have skill in bandaging and dressing, then if it recurs, as you did at first, do as you did before.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if the member does not respond to what we have said, then do not delay more than three days, or four, or seven, or twelve; and never longer than that, until the splint is broken and approaches the bone; therefore, tighten the restraint more than before, and the tissue will grow larger as I have said before; and if you see the member becoming drier than it should be, soak it with warm water every time you remove it, and do this every day, and cut away the norrissemens at the member; thus, the norrissemens will be removed from the member, and the wound will heal: this is harmful, and if it is not cured, then I know of no other remedy than constant lassification and proper overying.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of various kinds of wounding
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Many kinds of wounds are there, and various shapes, and the causes are assigned; for there are wounds made by the blow of a spear, and the whole bone is fractured as if it were a bone, like when it is cut or broken; and therefore this kind of wounding is called "fracture.
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Or the spear strikes the bone through various senses of the eye, and is called this kind of wounding "absolute"; and it is the wound of these two great or small fractures.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if it is a percussion that is impaled, or a cut or of piercing, or of the cheek under the pierce, or of other kinds.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	If there is a persistent fracture, which brings the skin that is exposed to the bone or it is on the bone, and this wound or large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	If there is a wound that is repaired in the bone as subtle as possible, and it is a small cut, and for this it is called this fracture "capillary"; and if the wound is made by injury, or by piercing, or by something seeming, and it lets the piece of the bone enter, and it is the same as when they heated the cauldrons when they were burned; if it enters through the hole.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And there are more cases of those who have moist bones, like that of a child; and they occur in all these ways of fracture that are lightly broken, like these; and I will speak of this in their language.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us consider all the ways of fractures by the methods used for them, and by the corruption of the char that is used.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of the capsule is known by the fact that when one discovers the bone, and rubs it with the finger, if the black fracture is open.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the fracture, keep a close watch on the patient, and if you see no accidents of the midwife, such as vomiting of cole, admission of understanding, extension, and pulsation, and fever, and the limbs to become red and swollen, and other similar signs in other cases, that cannot be cured with doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	If you do not see an accident, and you expect a cure, then begin it.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	When the bone comes first to you, and it is in the wrist, then it is necessary to cut the bone before the fortieth day of the month.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	If it is in this way, then if you cut the bone before the ninth month, then the skin of the bone must be corrupted, and the accident that we have mentioned will come.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	If the fracture of the bone comes to the skin that covers the eye, then it is necessary to cut the broken part if you want to: and it is that you pull the head of the malady that has been cut, and uncover the bone in all the ways that you can, and uncover the figure of the wound more than you can, and if the sanc comes out to reveal the bone, or the apothem, then help what must be done, and it is that you fill the eye with oiled powdered linen; and rest the wound as long as the sanc is calmed and assured of not deviating from its course, and then begin to cut the bone, and it is made according to two ways of incision: one way if the cut is narrow at the end, and it is in this form.
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	Then the other size is greater than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is if you have many sizes, some narrow and others wide, and they are sharp, and they are made of iron; and you perform them lightly so that you do not cut the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and thick, then you must pierce it through, otherwise, you must first make holes with needles, and they should not be too small, lest they go further into the bone; and there should be a margin or circle around each hole that does not pass over the bone; and you must have more holes, if every time you hit the bone with the edge of the needle, you have needles for your test; and this is the form of the three ways of needles:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality to perceive the broken bone is that you put the ice on the bone, and turn it as often as you can until you feel that the bone is perceived; then put the ice on another part a little later, and then do everything around, then cut as the incisions in the bone that is between the fingers, and do it as subtly as you can, and lightly, as we have said, as you touch the bone with your hand, or with any of the tools you have like needles, tweezers; and make sure you do not touch the skull or the face.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have perceived and treated the bone, if it comes that you resort to the instruments that are supposed to be like an incision, but it is more slender and subtle than the other incision; and if it does not cause any small bones, neither any scales, if the soft bones of the fingers are lightly touched with the tools we have mentioned, then cure the wound with tents and bandages that we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another way of opening is when it is said by the Galiens, who are more skilled; and the larger one, and that is their word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first to remove a part of the bone, where the fracture opening is wide, so that once you have removed this part, if you measure from the center of this incisional lenticular chief, then the form is:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut too much, and the part is torn in two, if the cutting is towards the bone; then gently press a small maillet on it, so that you lightly touch the whole bone, and be well guarded by the thread that is loose; if it is near the bone, if the bone is light, because it is easily injured, and causes pain.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture of the bone does not pierce through the skin, and the bone is only covered by muscles, and it has small pieces, then cover them with the rough asperity, and file the scales with a subtle raser, which you must have several quantities of, to meet the needs of each joint according to its type and the figure of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you sharpen before with coarse graters, and then with more subtle ones, and continue doing this as much as it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In every other hair removal and subtle fracture, it is necessary to meet the needs according to its address; and this is something that cannot be corrected for those who have studied in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	1. If the fracture is discovered, it comes to pass that you must preheat the linen according to the size of the wound, and apply olive oil, and place it on the wound; then take another doubled strip of linen, and apply vinegar and olive oil, and place it on the first strip; and do this more gently than you would, so as not to burn the flesh, and then administer by other strips, and do not strain it too much, only until the wound has healed enough; and leave it for one or two days, until the swelling is pacified, then remove it, and administer medicines such as these: roots of various kinds, flour of times, powder of incense, aristolochum, and similar things; and from these things make a powder, and place it on the wound, and administer subsequent medicines without suture; and guard that the wound be clean, so that you do not leave the ointment or bandage assembled on the skin, for if the bandage assembles on the skin, it can cause great harm to the patient; for if you place something moldy on the wound, it can cause great pain to the patient.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	If there is no accident coming to the patient, and if we have said so, then it is doubtful whether there is any danger.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if no harm comes from the medicine we have put on it, then a part of honey, three parts of rose oil, and one part of glue, and the rest is made of wax, should be applied; then the cure will be done in the manner of cures that it covers, as long as it is healthy.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	It is said that the two parts of the shoulder never break, or only one, because they are two bones; and this is cartilaginous, and does not break, unless it is bent or twisted, and then it becomes healthy.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, then you should cut off your small toe or nail and make the break even on your index finger, and in the pouch as long as it does not deviate from its natural figure; and do this lightly, and let the patient feel no pain through your guidance.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the part of the nail that cannot reach the toe, then you should put it even at the head of a large braid.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is in the second part, then you should repeat the first joint and restore the original toe, if possible; if not, after the ninth or tenth day, when the wound is healed, then cut off the tip of the nail, if the break is in a part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	When you cut one part, the other will also be cut; and if the wounds are large, they fill the cavities with pus.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And no restorer would say that you should smooth the wounds with a burr, and each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It seems to me that it is well, but they must be smoothed in the making of oakum and ground honey, and then leave the wound, as long as the bone is hard and the cartilage is tough.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And no time is it ever cut on the neck of the wound, and if it is soft and wrinkled, and holds the pressure, and blows the salves among; or as you have seen.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if the wound is infected, it comes to the nurse while you are working, if it has a cloth or cotton that has been oiled with lavender oil, or in a small bottle of alcohol.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is not infected, it does not come to the nurse while you are working, if it has a plaster made of flour and baking powder, and incense powder, mixed with fresh eggs, then put on light sponges, and do not tie the wound; and if the wound is small, and it is broken into small pieces, if it is not necessary to remove the stitches, then cut the fringe, and the cure of things enchanting charms, and soothing, as if plasters and ointments are suitable for this; and if there is no wound on the limb, if the limb is cured with tents, and puts on needles, as long as it is healthy.
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the dislocation of the lower jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the lower jaw is dislocated, there is no wound, and the fracture is not severe, and it does not break into pieces, but only slightly, and is not broken in two, but is bent slightly, if one knows, it can be straightened with slight force.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the fracture is in the right side of the jaw, to make the index of your left hand in the mouth of the patient; and if the fracture is on the left side of the jaw, then make the index of your right hand on the fracture, straighten it slightly, and fix it with the other hand, and hold it in place.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the lower jaw is healed in two parts, and it is equal, then you must administer extension for two parts.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the teeth move or fracture, and they are pulled by a gold, silver, or silk thread, then place the broken lower jaw end on the cervical fracture, and place one double cloth on it; and place another double cloth on the long and wide part of the jaw according to its size, and tie it to the patient's neck, and order the patient to lie down, and give them light food.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you see that the figure changes, and it drifts to another place, and then put it back in its place; and apply plaster on it, with flour from a mortar or milled flax, after you have osteit the cervical fracture; and apply light plaster on it, and when it sets, do not change its position, leave it as it is until it is healthy; several times it will be healthy in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	If the abscess pus comes out, then it is best not to force what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	If there is a fracture and multiple wounds, a small piece of bone from the leg is removed; if the osteon has flexible joints, it can be easily replaced.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	If the wound is wide, then enlarge it according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you have all the bones in place, and there is no pain, if the wound is wide, then make it large and put flexible bandages on it to support it until it heals.
de la forcele	Of the force
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The force breaks more often in the direction of the shoulder, and the break is in three ways: either it is broken and separated into two, and it has pieces, and it is the lighter to restore; or it is broken with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the evacuation is when the break is in the direction of the wound, that you have two ministers, if the one touches the helper that feels the force of the break; and the other extends the col towards the part; then set the break in your two hands, so that it forms as it should, and there should be no appearance or difference.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	If you have further work to do, place the shoulder blade of the patient on the table with a round or flat object made of cloth or linen, depending on your need; and hold it gently but firmly in your hand so that you can even out the break.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	If you do not dare to cut the head of the force off, because it comes out too far, and place the shoulder blade on your ear or the other side, and hold the muscles of the shoulder blade with your hand as long as the bone of the force is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then address the fracture to your two, and if you manage to remove the fragments, then sell them; and take care to lighten the pieces slightly, and if the bone cannot be joined by any overhang, it is because the instrument is not strong enough to separate the facies: but make sure to use the right force on this instrument to avoid damaging the face.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And it seems like a spoon, and is not too thin, and should be as wide as the bone desires, according to the size of the bone and the power of the hand; and if there are two heads, as you see, and some are large, and others are short, if it is the fracture of the wound that you made when you treated the bones; and when you are sure of the aposteme, if the wound is small, or you doubt the aposteme, if you use the wound with drapelz and tentes, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if the abscess opens, if it is filled with oil of rose and vinegar and wine, and it is closed.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	And the treatment of the bone is when it is painful and smaller than usual, and it is closed. Then take a large piece of powdered millnut and oak gall, and light sponges, and place a small ball at the end; then take a thin twist of three to four inches long and long, and wrap it around the bend; then place the twine on top of the sponges, so that the bend is held tight; then take a subtle twine of three to four inches long and long, and wind it around the bend while the bend is still tight; then turn the bend over the wrist, and tie the knot at the end of the bend, and soak the clean and sour salve, and soak the unsour salve; and remove the twine from each part, and when you see that the bend holds the wrist tightly, and you can clearly see that the twine does not move on the bone, and the restraint is tight; and make the mace lie on its side, and place it on the back of the mace, and lift the helper up when the patient falls asleep, or raise the shoulder to the collar, and do not dislocate the elbow or arm if it does not happen often, for at most 20 days; then resume the wrapping, if you see that it has value, and pull it and let it go as soon as it is restored; and it is restored in the most of 28 days, and in no fewer than any man.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Of the break of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement. de la brisure dou pis	of the break

de la brisure dou col	Of the break of the shoulder

de la brisure de l’ajutoire	Of the dislocation of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder joint is the bone that connects the upper arm to the shoulder blade, and if it is dislocated, then it must be reset according to one of the following two methods:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And the head of the shoulder is dislocated, and it is pulled back, and the patient's arm is held above the head; then the bone of the dislocated shoulder is pushed down until it reaches the elbow, and a small hinge is formed at the elbow, which can be bent in any direction or extended. Then the patient places their hands together, as the hinge returns to its original position.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other way is if one dislocates the patient's shoulder due to their anger, and holds their hand on their collar, then commands the ministers that they trace the one that is at the joint of their hands, and the others trace it without exception in all parts, and extend each to its part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part. And if the breach is near the shoulder blade, then it is necessary to place the joint on the middle of the shoulder, and the other on the elbow, so that when the breach is toward the elbow, and the shoulder blade, then place the breach, as you can, without labor, until the breach is equal at both places, and at both shoulders; then stretch the breach, as you can, and extract it, hold still without moving.

When the shoulder becomes inflamed and does not improve within seven days, and if it is not relieved by applying a poultice of moist herbs and olive oil, then it is best to strain it; then extract it, and the manner of extracting it is as follows: if you place the plaster on the wrist, then assemble the arm with the helper, and place your hand on the shoulder or on the chest; and then tighten the bandage, and extract it with the helper and with the arm, so that the arm is in its proper place, and nothing else will dislodge it, or if the bone does not move.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	1. And if you doubt that the bone does not move, then use these and place the incision on a larger and stronger needle than the others, and have one between each incision, and make sure each incision is as large as it can pass through the bone division three times; then draw out the needles, as I said at the beginning of this chapter, more forcefully and less by moving them away.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	1. And if you see the seat of the incisions and the bleeding, as we have said, in the part where you are restoring the broken limb, and you doubt the abscess, if it leaves the bone alone for seven days, as we have said; then look at each of the three days' link, that pruritus does not swell or come to the head because the fistula does not come to the limb due to being too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the address, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no accidents occur, but only if it is after three days or more, and the patient sleeps on his back, and has his hands on his stomach; and then place the assistant's hand plainly on the line, and look at each hour during the night or morning, to see which part of the broken limb does not move, or is not softened by the flesh; if the address is due to the power of medicine, and the meat that we have before us, in such a way that the meat is subtle; and when it comes back to take, if it is large.
