And it is customary that the helper and the leg should be re-taken in 40 days or more; therefore, one must gently and administer baths and medicines for ointments to the shoulder to improve it.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	2. And if the stricture is thick and blocked, it should be slowly unwrapped for 10 to 2 months.
de la brisure du bras	3. of the arm's fracture
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	4. The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "forearm" or "ulna," and one of them is thinner, and it is the part that holds the pouch; and the other is thicker, and it is the part that is longer, by chance, towards the smaller one; in case of breaking only one of the thinner bones or the thicker one, or both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the child's teeth are broken, the restorations are light, and the cures; and when the large ones are broken, it is the healing that is poor, and more painful than when they are broken individually.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is only the child's teeth that are broken, then it is sufficient to extend lightly and put equal.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the large teeth that are broken, then it should be tightened more strongly; and extend it over the thumb, and raise the palm of the other hand, and the teeth should be lower than the others, and let the mouth rest on its own cheek, and the thumbs raised in front of the other hand, or at the elbow, and some other parts on the opposite side.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	Then he places the head in its place, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it breaks into pieces, he puts each in its place, and if there are no loose pieces that point the way, and you cannot restore it to its place, then follow our advice and the bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the fracture there is a wound, I speak to the single cauterist; if he takes care of it.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if at the beginning of restoration there are gapes, and they are made of oil rose and black wax, neither too hard nor too soft, nor too thick; and they are draped subtly, as long as the gapes are pacified.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	Then take the cautery, and put the powder of the mill with a lot of urine on it, then make the holes, and let the wheat be larger than the others; and see if there are VI holes or arms in more positions: whether the wheat is in one of the bones, or in two; and draw it more under the wheat that is further away, as I said at the beginning of this chapter; and let the corners be that are under the wheat be wet and moist, and not too hard or rough; and let the string, which is drawn, be linen, not too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the member and the limb after some time.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any accidents come to the member, if it is like pricking to the member, if you heat the member with hot water as much as necessary until the pricking is relieved; and let the member rest in its place.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then continue the stretching, and if the limb is softened and the bones are exposed, and it seems like something, if it is alleviated.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the knots do not come to the member because it is too tight, for which reason you must loosen it as soon as possible, and let some time pass until the knots are untied, and then stretch it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things come to the patient's aid within twenty years, it is not good.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	If the dislocation is not corrected within thirty years, it becomes permanent; however, if it is corrected within thirty-five years or even in twenty years, depending on the composition and complexion of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the hand dislocation
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	It is said that on the back of the hand and in the wrist there are few dislocations, and only sprains many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And if the wrist of the hand is broken or sprained, it is said that the patient should lie down and straighten his arm in front of him evenly; then place his hand on the extended thigh, extend the broken bones, and put the fingers in their places as they are well joined; then apply plaster and bandages, if necessary, then wrap it according to the size of the leg; and then wrap it in a drape made of linen.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the cut is at the back of the abdomen, near the sole of the foot, I make a ball of cloth, and instruct the patient to scratch at the broken part; then I stretch out a long thread, and it should be as large as the sole of the foot, and I stretch it, as one does.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the cut is on the back of the hand, then it comes to pass that you put a bandage over it, and another under it, if the wrist is straight and in line, then the thumb turns inward between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the cut is not on either of the two, if they are closed, then it comes to pass that you put them in line, and if you see that you can raise the cut with the plantar, and if you look at the thumb, which is raised, and does not move; and if the cut is on other fingers, if it is on the index or one of the others, if it is closed, and the thumb is raised with the healthy one that follows; or you tie them all together, as much as you can, or you put a bandage over it, as one does; and take care in restoration and in the position of the wound, and cut what comes, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	Of the broken joint
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The bone of the joint is often broken in two places, and it can be seen when it turns front and back; the restoration is if it lies on the line of the fracture, and the other side is dislocated.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient groans when it is their turn, then extends each of the muscles that connect to the bone in its proper place; and this is when the fracture occurs.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the fracture is near the root of the joint, then some of the ligaments turn towards the point of pain, and the others turn away from the fracture.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And as it has come to the joint, and therefore the ligaments of the joint should be released, and the extension should be equal; then place the bone in its proper position with your hands, according to its natural figure, and then apply the splint, and the bandage, and do not let it move.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if it has been strained, and you let it rest, then return to your care and your home; the bandage is made in a certain way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap it around the ankle, doubled in two or three, and remove any excess, then bend the leg until the heel reaches the root of the nail, and tie the long end between the thigh and the leg, releasing the ankle joint; then bend the leg and the thigh the bandage, then put on the brace and one on the bone of the leg; then place the leather between the leg and the thigh to put the strain in its proper position, and begin to tie three or four turns on the brace; and as more you use the brace, and less it is tightened; then take out the two ends of the thread that you have tied between the leg and the thigh, and the three or four turns that are on the brace, then return to the ankle joint and see if it is still tight; the strain, if it does not move from its place, then let it go, then leave it, then it will not apostheme nor enflame nor any other sign.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	If it happens, if it does not respond, and address what comes, as we have said many times; and if it has pieces of bone that prick, if possible, and it can; and if it cannot, then it is necessary to cut the limb, and drain it; and the cure, as we have said, depending on how healthy it is.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And no time is the joint broken when one puts it in place, as in the shoulder and arm; however, in the restoration made afterward, it does not clash with the patient's pain.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	You should know that the joint is restored in L days, or less or more, according to the differences in complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	From the rule of the right knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	It is said that in the right knee joint there is little breaking, but it cracks many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, whether it is only a scratch or a puncture, and all the wounds appear, and they feel painful, and this is not good.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is when you put back what has been lost on both sides as much as possible, and then the template is placed, and an adjusted nail is inserted, if you have the skill, and it is tightened as it should be, then all the adjustments we have made for other fractures are rewarded, such as a broken hip and other similar appearances; if you put back what is necessary for each accident, as much as possible, then it will be healthy.
de la brisure de la jambe	Of the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	There are two bones in the leg, and some are called "true" by right, not "weasel," and the others are called "foscile." And all fractures are like that of the arm, and for this the restoration is done in the same way as that of the arm. And if the two bones are broken together, then turn the leg from all sides.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the delicate bones are broken, then turn forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bones are broken, then it causes great pain and one sees well; then turn away.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Adonques, ensure proper extension and align it evenly; however, be aware that the fracture may be uneven, and there may be more pieces, which will make the extension less severe and lighter. Follow your strength.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your incision, if you take two strips of twisted hair that prick the leg on both sides and are long enough to reach from the knee to the ankle, then wrap them around the leg and tie them at both ends, and place the end of the strip under the joint and tie it there, and do not allow the leg to deviate to the side or the other, and it is well; and no one has caused pain in the leg, and it was made of twisted hair, and you put it on to prevent movement, and properly made it in the fracture or wound; and move each leg every day to see if there is any swelling or other accident; if the cure is as healthy as possible.
de la brisure des os dou piet	Of the fracture of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, there is no fracture, but the bones of the foot never break, and they must be very hard to break, and have only been broken in more positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if the bones of the foot are broken and you see the bones slipping over each other, if they are so hard pressed against the ground, just as if they were flying, then now place your foot on the other leg, lift the one that is broken, press it as much as it will become in its place; then place the splint and stitch it, and cut the belly of the foot a little table at the ankle, then draw it up to the knee, then wrap the cloth around, and other things that you have skill for.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	When three or four days have passed, if the bone is not healed, you will find the bones unevenly broken and dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	If there are two fractures, if they heal, then as we have said, you must use the other hand; then place a splint on the longer of the two, and make it slightly larger, then place the pin in the wound that I mentioned, and tighten the strap; and if there are II or III, or more, fractures, if you place one on each, according to its quantity, wrapped in one layer of linen, and draw the strap tight around the pin; and make sure that the head of the splint is positioned against the abdomen of the wound, so that it fits well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And it is necessary that you do not overlook the other things I have said for other injuries, as soon as we have said them; and attend to each accident as we have said.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the bone of the shoulder
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the woman's shoulder bone is broken, if it is made to be large, then it bends towards the side of the shoulder, and is held by the side; then fill the nature of the woman with cloth, and put it in as much as possible; then lift the woman's shoulder, and gently bend the back a little at a time, and when it comes to the entrance of the nature, and returns with the cloth, if she sees blood, if the cloth is saturated, re-insert it, and make seven turns or more: if the fracture is restored, and if you see, take a bucket of herbs, and tie a cord to the mouth, and blow all the bucket into the nature; then let the cord be exhaled from the nature: the nature will return to the fracture; then fill it with cloth, and leave it alone for some time until it is healthy.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	When the bone of the elbow is broken, or of the woman, if it is restored as we have said in the elbow of the hawk; and these breaks are not hidden that much from the one who studies and uses it, and understands my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the break means in more ways the right way of restoration: understand the dough.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the same way, when it is broken, take an ostrich gullet and bite the limb; then wrap it with drapes, and leave it for three days or so, and it will be cured quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	Of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for the one who has a fracture with wound, just as it is large, if it is like the bone of the shoulder or elbow, or seems so, that it is now healthy, if the wounds that we have said testify to it.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the healthy wound is, if the inflammation of vitrol increases, if you have nothing else, then continue to restore the fracture at the same hour, or the next day, if the swelling does not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if the swelling increases and comes out, if you leave the restoration for the next day, as long as the inflammation is calmed, and do not touch it again on the third or fourth day, because you will cause bad luck to come.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the bone is broken, it should be set as soon as possible, so that you can gently place it at your fingertips, in slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if you cannot easily extend the bone, use this instrument made of iron, which is seven or eight feet long, and its size corresponds to the size of the wound; for this reason, it is necessary to make three or four cuts, according to the number of cuts needed in each case of fracture; it should be sharp and large, so that it does not tear at the compression of the member on your thumb, and should be larger in front, and large in the environment in front.
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "bandage", because it is necessary that the heads of the bones be placed on the top of the bone; and it should be once, as soon as it rises, and be even on one side of the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is slight, and the splints cannot hold the bone well, then it comes that you cover the top of the bone with the splint, as long as the splints are in place.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you do not return the bone to its place, as we have said, if it is covered with an instrument that is suitable for this, or cutting and sharp, then you should use this tool that has been removed from the hard parts and small scratches in the bone.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is reset, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, be advised that it is not natural in its original state.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If you work on it until it is in its original position, then wrap it in a strip of black vinegar cloth, and do it properly as such; and do not put anything on the wound or elsewhere that has oil, so that it does not become infected and corrupted; then after restoring the bone, administer remedies as you see fit, and leave the wound exposed, covering it completely according to the size of the wound, and take good care that the wound is not tightened with the fracture; and many times have I seen this work well, and have caused the patient to come out of the pain or die or corrode never; and so the scars are more moist and softer than the other scars.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is large or severe, and you doubt that it will come to harm as we have said, but if there is pain in the limb, then do not tighten too much; instead, wrap it loosely, around the limb, hard knots, and tie them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after I or II days that the wound has healed completely, and if all you have used is the remedy on the wound, and you use a salve for painful wounds, like a medicinal ointment and similar things.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary to unwrap the limb twice a day, in the morning and evening, as long as it is tight and healthy.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	It is necessary that the limb be aligned in a way that the belly is covered lightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if they continue to press, and it cannot be fastened but pulled away from the belly, with small pieces of bones, because it can cause the wound to open, and all these pieces that bring about this pain, you must treat them with care.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if the fistula comes to the hip, or in another way of corruption, and you must treat it according to what is said in this chapter before.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and exposed through the limb, as if it were the bone of the elbow or shoulder, and other similar bones of the large limbs, if you do not treat it, because often it dies; by chance it may heal after 20 or 30 years, and then treat the wound, if you can; and if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	Of the blisters that come out with heat
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We come often after the healing of the wound, moreover when it is near the joint, and one must see the figure of the member; and by chance it cannot make the members its natural way.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	If the wound is fresh: if it is treated with warming medicines, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocolle, acacia, and other similar things, whether you use any of these or all together, and mix them with warming ointment or with an excess of urine or with vinegar; and then apply them to the wound in poultices, and draw them out well, and do not let them drop from your hands; and then draw them out again, and continue another one as long as the swelling remains; or you draw out a piece of plaster well made; for the property of the plaster is that it all presses together all the flaps of the members; and if the swelling has already become hard like a piercing, and it is sore to the bone, if the raseur is put on, and the superfluity is removed; or you leave it without any raseur, as long as it is sore, and the cure as long as it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	A limb that is weak after imprisonment
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the bone fracture is healed, and weakens after the weak limbs and subtly, if it happens for various reasons: either because the one was too tightly bound, and was not well tied; or because it received too many stitches, and could not come to the nails at the member; or due to multiple swelling; or because there were too many movements, not in its time; or because it had little blood in its heart, and is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is if you make the patient lie on his back and tighten the cloth around him as much as possible so that there are no multiplications in him; then give him a bath, and he will feel relieved and relaxed; then put powder on the limb, if it attracts the great swelling, and the inflammation often comes from the knee; and revive to his natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	A dislocated limb after the healing process
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is swollen after restoration, and the bones are broken open, and the disfigured limb is crooked, it does not resemble its natural shape: if one does not believe the folk who say that the bone must be broken all at once, and most of them have done this in our land; and these bones are blamed, and great harm comes to them, and by chance they die; however, if the wounds and tortures are fresh, and if they are washed with hot water or herbs that are mollified, as if they were made of viscous substance, or roots, and honey, and similar things; and I apply a mollifying ointment, as if it were well made, and I take the viscous substance of vismalve, and cook it with animal fat or olive oil, and apply it thusly; or I take fat figs, and roast them with fish sauce, and similar medicines that dry the sweat.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And no time is there where the node does not occur due to continuous and long pressure with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And let there be no movement in the limb at any hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twisting is aroused and made painful, as well as the incision, and it is necessary to use iron on the bone, if it comes close to the bone, with a subtle and light cut; and then rest and study in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocations occur when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to none, if it comes now to bring sense to the target.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if we delay, if we read it, and by chance if we reset it on the shoulder; because no one can move the joint when it is inflamed: many times brought pain and other aches: always, when this happens, I make the patient healthier with ointment and then let him, as long as the abscess is healed, apply warm oil and oil to the limb, then reset it lightly, and cure each limb as we have cured it in its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	I have ordered the surgeons for the dislocation of the shoulder joints.
des mandibules	for the mandibles
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	There are times when the mandibles are dislocated, and the dislocations of both are in two ways: either they are a small piece of their bones, and become soft; or they are completely dislocated, and hang down towards the chest, and cut off the saliva from the mouth that cannot hold it, and cannot close the mouth, and wrap around the tongue with the speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	If the dislocation is small, it returns through more positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	1. If it is complete and accomplished, if you reset it as soon as possible, and without force; in such a way that the master of the assistant marks the chief of the patient's shoulder, and bites the tip of one of his hands at the root of the dislocation of the mandible which covers the mouth, if it is dislocated by 2 parts; and the other two hands are deformed, to be equal; and command the patient to smooth his jawbones, his mandibles, and move them from all sides.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	2. And the teeth are set in their place, as they should be in his jaw.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	If the dislocation is returned to its place, it should be done gently, just as it is the two mandibles together, if the hot and oily drips do not cause any harm; do not force too hard when returning it, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	If the dislocation is returned to its place correctly, and the patient's mouth feels relieved, then apply soft cotton fluff made of olive oil and wax gently around the mouth; let the patient lie on his back, and keep his head between his knees so that he does not move to the left or right, and do not force himself to vomit, but chew gently as long as the pain is steady and does not affect the jaws; then take what has been gently applied and do not try to open the mouth with your fingers and drink, as long as the jaw is well healed and healthy.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two mandibles cannot be set in place within an hour and are not converted to their original position, and if fever and customary aches come, and by chance a solution of the belly, and by chance vomiting of clear water.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, you will know that it is a disaster; and many have died in nine years.
de la forcelle	of force
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The force cannot be overcome by the cost of continuing the effort and the pain, and it is never unstable at the end, but it is well felt.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is when the patient lies down on his back and extends his arms; then press your palm against the shoulder, it will return; then place the splint and bandage, and tighten; and the part that is towards the elbow cannot be dislocated, not even if it is not stable once, and if it does not become unstable again, as we have said; then place the splint and bandage, and tighten, and command the patient to rest until he is healthy; and then, when the head of the shoulder is dislocated, bring the children back to their mother as soon as the shoulder is in its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	There are three ways in which the shoulder is dislocated: either it is dislocated at the head of the humerus bone at the shoulder socket; or it is dislocated at the top of the shoulder blade; or it is dislocated at the side, and this happens rarely; and it does not dislocate the arm, nor does it dislocate the nerves; and more often it dislocates towards the shoulder socket, especially for those who have little strength, because they fall greatly; for those who have enough strength, it falls with a few steps, and returns with a few steps.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance, it happens to some men that they are struck or cut, and the muscle of their arm is torn away from the shoulder, and make sure it is not dislocated.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	It is necessary that you examine it, as long as you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And know the dislocations when they are towards the axis, and make a difference between the diseased shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find between them a manifest difference; and you will find at the top of the shoulder a hollow, and from there to the head of the shoulder, as if it were some ones; and the patient cannot bring his hand back to its place, and make no movements; and also, if it is dislocated upwards, if it is not hidden, because you can see it manifestly at the head; and this way of dislocation is not hard to restore, when it is new, or if the muscle is diseased.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	The manner is that the minister lightly places his hand on the shoulder of the sick person, then takes your hands and extends them upwards, placing them apart; he lightly applies pressure to the joint at the top of the shoulder; he then removes his hand and extends it upwards, putting it aside; if he comes hastily.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said in our hands just after, if the patient is to be bathed in hot water; and he is gently relaxed and soothed, as with a decoction of aloe and fenugreek and honey in hot water, and is relaxed; then he is lowered on his back, and one place his hand on the shoulder of the patient, not too soft nor too hard, then places his foot on the hand of the patient's sole, and lightly holds the shoulder girdle, and draws the hand of the minister; and other ministers trace the shoulder girdle, if it does not move; this shoulder returns now, and if you see that it is held in this manner: and that you cause the present home to be greater than the shoulders; and that it is turned towards the chest, and bend the shoulder away from the shoulder of the patient, and hold the shoulder up, so that the shoulder hangs down in the armpit; and other ministers trace the hand of the patient towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	If the patient is too light, if there is nothing heavy for them to bear with it, the dislocation returns now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And the reduction is also done in another way: and it is like this: the shoulder is placed as if it were a pilaster, and it is not too thick or too rough; then it is put back into the patient's shoulder, but if it has slipped out too far, and the shoulder is too long, then the hand is formed on the other side, and the joint returns to its place in the arm; and if it does not return after all these things that we have said, then this treatment must be followed: take two shoulder bones of large size and four of wide size, which have the head entered from the front of the shoulder, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then lie the head of the wrist is loosened and tied, that it may not catch the maid's hand, then place the bandage around the maid's wrist; and extend some of the arms over the long wrist, and the helper over the shoulder of the arm, then put the arm over I eschilon of a large shield, and extend the hands on the other side, and let the chest hang down from another part: the joint is now relieved.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is done, in whatever way that may be, if you find that you must place the bandage a spider's thread equal, then place the powdered flour dust with incense and wool of oven all over the shoulder and chest, then tighten the knot around the bandage again, and turn the cord on the powder, and tie the hand on the arm, and let the hands remain still.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	1. It is necessary that he drink little at first, as long as the limb is comfortable, because it will heal faster; then gradually increase after the first four or seven days, and move it; and if it is tight and does not soften, it is healthy.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	2. If the joint is tight due to moisture or for another reason, it is necessary that you administer cauteries at three points, as it is placed in front of or in the chapter of cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	3. If you do all this, and after seven weeks, the joint still does not hold and cannot raise the arm forward, then you should suspect that the nerve at the top of the shoulder is compressed or extended or softened; and suspect that the joint will never fit in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The first line of the text translates to: "The dislocation that is towards the foot, and the ankles, or knees, if it is made by impulse and extension of hands, and it is treated another time; and cure until it is healthy.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And after the cure comes pain in the member, and then movement, if the patient uses cold water many times, as long as that pain is not alleviated, and then it should return to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dear dislocation
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	It is said that when the stiff joint is dislocated, it repeatedly returns to its place, and all parts are dislocated; and it becomes dislocated from front to back, and the dislocations are not well rejoined, as they can be seen and felt; and it becomes dislocated according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	When you join the male member with your hand, if you see it open.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is weak, and cannot grip the arm, nor touch the shoulder with anything.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary to reset it always with the help of a lever, because if it is not reset, it will be painful to return; and by chance it cannot be returned at all, even when it is in place; rather than other dislocations, it is more painful, and by chance it can cause death.

Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The big toe is never used, and it is never fully dislocated, and it is bent and twisted.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the sign is if the ankle is swollen, and it should be checked before the part where it is dislocated: the fingers are light, and it should be gently stretched with the hands as it is only weak.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is completely dislocated, if the ankle is checked before the part where it is dislocated: the fingers are light, and it should be gently stretched with the hands as it is only weak. Then seat the patient on the right side, and with the left hand pull the leg towards you; then take the knee in your right hand, and then in the left twice, and raise it up, and hold it well at the top of the knee; and do this twice, if we have said, by bending and raising the knee; if it returns, it is well; if not, if it does not return, repeat the treatment, as it will return; and if it cannot return again, then make the patient lie on his back on the ground, and keep the knee firmly on the ground between the thighs, and let it dangle freely, so that the knee does not bend; then mark the ministers with the knee, and some others extend the dislocation to the hands or the leg, where the knee is located; then stretch them equally, and the passus should be held between the knees to hold the knee; then put the dislocation in your hands, and mark the healthy leg at the ankle, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	When it reaches the point, if he applies plaster and allows it to dry, and forms the bandage, and ties it to the leg, and covers the nerves that are near the ankle bone, where the laces are too tight; then he leaves it on for II to III days, and if it remains tight, then it should be loosened; then he removes it at the end of the third or fourth day, and applies a new one every four days; and if it still does not improve, it is better to seek medical attention immediately.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the wound becomes inflamed and comes, then it is necessary to calm it down if possible, as we have said elsewhere, until it is healthy.
des dois	Of two kinds
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When they are dislocated, if they can be extended gently and easily, it is a light thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in no doubt or pain, then you should make the patient lie on his back or side, and place your hand on the joints, then press with your thumb until it pops; and when it is reduced, and it does not pop, then place the heel of your hand on the top of the knee, and press firmly, and hold for three seconds, and then release; and let him rest, until he is safe.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	Of wounds and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with a dislocation, and it is seen to be restored, often the patient dies: if you are not presumptuous in your cure, if you are not unskilled or merciful and slow, and if you are pitiful, do not be presumptuous; and use at the beginning of things soothing remedies for boils, and leave the patient in God's hand, if you see no hope of health; and when you see hope, then reset the limb to the shoulder, and if the boil is coming out, and the skin is dry, and the wound is healing, and the pain is less, and the bones are not broken, do what we have said in simple diseases; and do not enter into a way of despairing, according to what we have said, for this is according to your Creator's will, and for the knowledge of your heart and courage.
